⚡ Compute Services

AWS Compute services provide the infrastructure to run your anihpj Django application. This section covers EC2 for virtual machines, Lambda for serverless functions, Elastic Beanstalk for managed deployments, and Fargate for containerized workloads. Learn how to deploy and manage your jobpost application models (Skills, Author, Location, User, JobPost) across different compute platforms.

💡 Django Focus: This documentation shows practical examples of deploying the anihpj Django project to AWS Compute services using the AWS CLI, Docker containers, and pytest for testing the jobpost app models.

Amazon EC2 (Elastic Compute Cloud)

Virtual servers in the cloud for deploying Django applications

📋 EC2 Overview

Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud (EC2) provides resizable compute capacity in the cloud. It allows you to deploy your anihpj Django application on virtual machines with full control over networking, storage, and security. EC2 instances run your jobpost application with models for Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost data.

Core EC2 Operations for Django Deployment

run-instances - Launch new EC2 instances
describe-instances - Get instance information
start-instances - Start stopped instances
stop-instances - Stop running instances
terminate-instances - Delete instances
reboot-instances - Restart instances
create-security-group - Create firewall rules
authorize-security-group-ingress - Allow inbound traffic

run-instances

Launches one or more EC2 instances for your Django application. This creates new virtual machine instances in AWS that will host your jobpost application with Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost models.

Syntax
aws ec2 run-instances \
  --image-id {ami-id} \
  --count {count} \
  --instance-type {instance-type} \
  --key-name {key-name} \
  --security-group-ids {security-group-id} \
  --subnet-id {subnet-id} \
  --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value={value}}]'
Parameters Description
  • --image-id (string, required): The ID of the AMI (Amazon Machine Image) to use. Example: ami-0c55b159cbfafe1f0 for Amazon Linux 2 with Docker pre-installed
  • --count (integer): Number of instances to launch. Default: 1. For Django app with HA, use 2-3
  • --instance-type (string): Type of instance (t2.micro, t2.small, t3.medium, etc.). For development use t2.micro (free tier), for production use t3.medium or larger
  • --key-name (string, required): Name of the EC2 Key Pair for SSH access
  • --security-group-ids (list): List of security group IDs to apply to the instance
  • --subnet-id (string): VPC Subnet ID where instance will be launched
  • --tag-specifications (string): Tags to apply to resources (Key=Name,Value=anihpj-django-server)
  • --user-data (string): Base64-encoded user data script to run on instance startup (for installing Docker, Python, Django)
Return Value
  • Instances (Array): Information about the newly created instances
  • InstanceId (string): Unique identifier for the instance
  • State (string): Current state (pending, running, stopped, terminated)
  • PublicIpAddress (string): Public IP address for accessing the instance
5 Detailed EC2 Examples
Example 1: Launch t2.micro Django Development Server

Launch a single t2.micro EC2 instance for development and testing of the anihpj jobpost application. This is ideal for development environments and uses the free tier.

#!/bin/bash
# Launch t2.micro development instance
aws ec2 run-instances \
  --image-id ami-0c55b159cbfafe1f0 \
  --count 1 \
  --instance-type t2.micro \
  --key-name anihpj-dev-key \
  --security-group-ids sg-0123456789abcdef0 \
  --subnet-id subnet-0123456789abcdef0 \
  --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-jobpost-dev},{Key=Environment,Value=development}]' \
  --region us-east-1
{ "Instances": [ { "InstanceId": "i-0987654321fedcba0", "ImageId": "ami-0c55b159cbfafe1f0", "InstanceType": "t2.micro", "State": { "Code": 0, "Name": "pending" }, "LaunchTime": "2025-01-11T14:23:45.000Z", "PublicIpAddress": "54.123.45.67", "PrivateIpAddress": "10.0.1.50", "SecurityGroups": [ { "GroupId": "sg-0123456789abcdef0", "GroupName": "django-app-sg" } ], "Tags": [ { "Key": "Name", "Value": "anihpj-jobpost-dev" }, { "Key": "Environment", "Value": "development" } ] } ] }

Example 2: Launch t3.medium Production Django Server with User Data

Launch a t3.medium EC2 instance configured with Docker, Python, Django, and PostgreSQL for production deployment of the anihpj jobpost application. Includes automatic setup script.

#!/bin/bash
# Create user data script for automatic setup
USER_DATA=$(cat <<'EOF'
#!/bin/bash
# Update system packages
yum update -y

# Install Docker
amazon-linux-extras install docker -y
systemctl start docker
systemctl enable docker
usermod -a -G docker ec2-user

# Install Python 3.11 and pip
yum install python3.11 python3.11-pip -y

# Install PostgreSQL client
yum install postgresql -y

# Clone Django project
cd /home/ec2-user
git clone https://github.com/yourusername/anihpj-jobpost.git
cd anihpj-jobpost

# Install Django dependencies
pip3.11 install -r requirements.txt

# Run migrations for Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost models
python manage.py migrate

# Collect static files
python manage.py collectstatic --noinput

# Start Django development server
python manage.py runserver 0.0.0.0:8000 &
EOF
)

# Base64 encode user data
USER_DATA_B64=$(echo -n "$USER_DATA" | base64)

# Launch t3.medium production instance
aws ec2 run-instances \
  --image-id ami-0c55b159cbfafe1f0 \
  --count 1 \
  --instance-type t3.medium \
  --key-name anihpj-prod-key \
  --security-group-ids sg-0987654321abcdef0 \
  --subnet-id subnet-0987654321abcdef0 \
  --iam-instance-profile Name=anihpj-ec2-role \
  --user-data "$USER_DATA_B64" \
  --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-jobpost-prod},{Key=Environment,Value=production},{Key=App,Value=jobpost}]' \
  --monitoring Enabled=true \
  --region us-east-1
{ "Instances": [ { "InstanceId": "i-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8", "ImageId": "ami-0c55b159cbfafe1f0", "InstanceType": "t3.medium", "State": { "Code": 0, "Name": "pending" }, "LaunchTime": "2025-01-11T14:35:22.000Z", "PublicIpAddress": "54.234.56.78", "PrivateIpAddress": "10.0.2.100", "Monitoring": { "State": "enabled" }, "IamInstanceProfile": { "Arn": "arn:aws:iam::123456789012:instance-profile/anihpj-ec2-role" }, "Tags": [ { "Key": "Name", "Value": "anihpj-jobpost-prod" }, { "Key": "Environment", "Value": "production" }, { "Key": "App", "Value": "jobpost" } ] } ] }
# Django Production Instance Setup Status from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost from django.contrib.auth.models import User as DjangoUser # After user data script executes, the instance will have: production_config = { 'instance_id': 'i-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8', 'instance_type': 't3.medium', 'public_ip': '54.234.56.78', 'private_ip': '10.0.2.100', 'monitoring': 'enabled', 'software_stack': [ 'Docker Engine', 'Python 3.11', 'Django 5.2.5', 'PostgreSQL Client', 'Git' ], 'models_migrated': True } # Create initial admin user (via migration script) admin_user = DjangoUser.objects.create_superuser( username='admin', email='admin@anihpj.com', password='secure_password' ) # Create sample Skills skill1 = Skills.objects.create(name='Python', level='Advanced') skill2 = Skills.objects.create(name='Django', level='Advanced') skill3 = Skills.objects.create(name='AWS', level='Intermediate') print(f"Created {Skills.objects.count()} skills") # Output: Created 3 skills # Create sample Location location = Location.objects.create( city='San Francisco', state='California', country='USA', zip_code='94105' ) print(f"Locations in database: {Location.objects.count()}") # Output: Locations in database: 1 # Create sample Author author = Author.objects.create( user=admin_user, bio='Senior Python Developer', location=location ) print(f"Authors: {Author.objects.count()}") # Output: Authors: 1
Example 3: Launch 2 t3.small Instances for HA Django Cluster

Launch two t3.small instances in different availability zones for high availability deployment of the jobpost application with load balancing.

#!/bin/bash
# Launch 2 t3.small instances for HA cluster
aws ec2 run-instances \
  --image-id ami-0c55b159cbfafe1f0 \
  --count 2 \
  --instance-type t3.small \
  --key-name anihpj-ha-key \
  --security-group-ids sg-0123456789abcdef0 \
  --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-jobpost-ha},{Key=Environment,Value=production},{Key=Cluster,Value=primary},{Key=App,Value=jobpost}]' \
  --placement 'AvailabilityZone=us-east-1a' \
  --monitoring Enabled=true \
  --region us-east-1 \
  --output json > ha-instances.json

# Also launch one more in different AZ
aws ec2 run-instances \
  --image-id ami-0c55b159cbfafe1f0 \
  --count 1 \
  --instance-type t3.small \
  --key-name anihpj-ha-key \
  --security-group-ids sg-0123456789abcdef0 \
  --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-jobpost-ha-backup},{Key=Environment,Value=production},{Key=Cluster,Value=backup}]' \
  --placement 'AvailabilityZone=us-east-1b' \
  --monitoring Enabled=true \
  --region us-east-1
{ "Instances": [ { "InstanceId": "i-0abc1def2ghi3jk4", "InstanceType": "t3.small", "State": { "Name": "pending" }, "PublicIpAddress": "54.145.67.89", "PrivateIpAddress": "10.0.1.25", "Placement": { "AvailabilityZone": "us-east-1a" }, "Tags": [ { "Key": "Name", "Value": "anihpj-jobpost-ha" }, { "Key": "Cluster", "Value": "primary" } ] }, { "InstanceId": "i-0xyz9abc8def7ghi", "InstanceType": "t3.small", "State": { "Name": "pending" }, "PublicIpAddress": "54.156.78.90", "PrivateIpAddress": "10.0.1.26", "Placement": { "AvailabilityZone": "us-east-1a" }, "Tags": [ { "Key": "Name", "Value": "anihpj-jobpost-ha" }, { "Key": "Cluster", "Value": "primary" } ] } ] } # Secondary instance in different AZ: { "Instances": [ { "InstanceId": "i-0lmn5opq6rst7uvw", "InstanceType": "t3.small", "State": { "Name": "pending" }, "PublicIpAddress": "54.234.90.12", "PrivateIpAddress": "10.0.2.30", "Placement": { "AvailabilityZone": "us-east-1b" }, "Tags": [ { "Key": "Name", "Value": "anihpj-jobpost-ha-backup" }, { "Key": "Cluster", "Value": "backup" } ] } ] }
# HA Cluster Django Model Distribution from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost # HA Cluster configuration cluster_nodes = { 'primary_az': { 'instances': [ 'i-0abc1def2ghi3jk4', # anihpj-jobpost-ha (10.0.1.25) 'i-0xyz9abc8def7ghi' # anihpj-jobpost-ha (10.0.1.26) ], 'public_ips': ['54.145.67.89', '54.156.78.90'], 'availability_zone': 'us-east-1a', 'role': 'primary' }, 'backup_az': { 'instances': [ 'i-0lmn5opq6rst7uvw' # anihpj-jobpost-ha-backup (10.0.2.30) ], 'public_ips': ['54.234.90.12'], 'availability_zone': 'us-east-1b', 'role': 'backup' } } # Distributed database replication # Primary instances sync with backup for failover # Example queries across the cluster: all_skills = Skills.objects.all().values_list('id', 'name', 'level') # Output on all 3 instances: (initially empty) # Create location across cluster locations = Location.objects.bulk_create([ Location(city='New York', state='NY', country='USA'), Location(city='Los Angeles', state='CA', country='USA'), Location(city='Chicago', state='IL', country='USA'), ]) print(f"Created {len(locations)} locations") # Output: Created 3 locations # Check replication status on backup backup_locations = Location.objects.all().count() print(f"Backup node has {backup_locations} locations") # Output: Backup node has 3 locations
Example 4: Launch GPU Instance for ML Model Training

Launch a GPU-enabled instance (g4dn.xlarge) for training machine learning models on job recommendations and skill matching for the jobpost application.

#!/bin/bash
# Launch GPU instance for ML training
aws ec2 run-instances \
  --image-id ami-0c55b159cbfafe1f0 \
  --count 1 \
  --instance-type g4dn.xlarge \
  --key-name anihpj-ml-key \
  --security-group-ids sg-0456789012abcdef0 \
  --iam-instance-profile Name=anihpj-ml-role \
  --block-device-mappings '[{DeviceName:/dev/xvda,Ebs:{VolumeSize=100,VolumeType=gp3,DeleteOnTermination=true}}]' \
  --tag-specifications 'ResourceType=instance,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=anihpj-ml-trainer},{Key=Purpose,Value=skill-matching-ml},{Key=GPU,Value=enabled}]' \
  --monitoring Enabled=true \
  --region us-east-1

# Wait for instance to be in running state
aws ec2 wait instance-running --instance-ids i-0p9o8n7m6l5k4j3i2 --region us-east-1
{ "Instances": [ { "InstanceId": "i-0p9o8n7m6l5k4j3i2", "InstanceType": "g4dn.xlarge", "State": { "Name": "pending" }, "PublicIpAddress": "54.245.123.45", "PrivateIpAddress": "10.0.3.50", "BlockDeviceMappings": [ { "DeviceName": "/dev/xvda", "Ebs": { "VolumeId": "vol-0123456789abcdef0", "VolumeSize": 100, "VolumeType": "gp3", "Status": "attaching" } } ], "GpuDevices": [ { "Count": 1, "Name": "NVIDIA Tesla T4", "Memory": 16000 } ], "Tags": [ { "Key": "Name", "Value": "anihpj-ml-trainer" }, { "Key": "Purpose", "Value": "skill-matching-ml" }, { "Key": "GPU", "Value": "enabled" } ] } ] } # Instance is starting up with: # - GPU: NVIDIA Tesla T4 (16GB VRAM) # - vCPUs: 4 # - Memory: 16 GiB # - Storage: 100 GiB gp3 SSD
# ML Training Instance for Job Recommendation Model from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost from django.db.models import Count, Q # ML Instance training data preparation training_config = { 'instance_id': 'i-0p9o8n7m6l5k4j3i2', 'instance_type': 'g4dn.xlarge', 'gpu': 'NVIDIA Tesla T4 (16GB)', 'training_purpose': 'Job recommendation ML model', 'models_used': ['Skills', 'User', 'JobPost', 'Author'] } # Prepare training data from Django models # Get all skills for feature encoding all_skills = Skills.objects.all() print(f"Total skills in dataset: {all_skills.count()}") # Output: Total skills in dataset: 0 # Get all job posts for training labels job_posts = JobPost.objects.prefetch_related('author', 'location', 'required_skills').all() print(f"Available job posts for training: {job_posts.count()}") # Output: Available job posts for training: 0 # Prepare job posts by location (geographic features for ML) jobs_by_location = JobPost.objects.values('location__city').annotate(count=Count('id')).order_by('-count') print("Jobs by location distribution:") for loc in jobs_by_location: print(f" {loc['location__city']}: {loc['count']} jobs") # Output: (empty initially) # Prepare skills frequency in job posts skill_frequency = Skills.objects.annotate(job_count=Count('jobpost')).order_by('-job_count') print("\nMost required skills:") for skill in skill_frequency[:10]: print(f" {skill.name}: {skill.job_count} jobs") # Output: (empty initially) # ML feature engineering from User and Author data authors_with_skills = Author.objects.filter(skills__isnull=False).distinct().count() print(f"\nAuthors with skills: {authors_with_skills}") # Output: Authors with skills: 0
Example 5: Launch Spot Instance with Custom VPC and Networking

Launch a spot instance for cost-effective development of jobpost application with custom VPC, security groups, and network interface configuration.

#!/bin/bash
# Create custom VPC for jobpost app (if not exists)
VPC_ID=$(aws ec2 create-vpc --cidr-block 10.0.0.0/16 --region us-east-1 --query 'Vpc.VpcId' --output text)

# Create subnet
SUBNET_ID=$(aws ec2 create-subnet --vpc-id $VPC_ID --cidr-block 10.0.1.0/24 --region us-east-1 --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' --output text)

# Create security group for Django application
SG_ID=$(aws ec2 create-security-group \
  --group-name anihpj-jobpost-sg \
  --description "Security group for anihpj jobpost Django app" \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --region us-east-1 \
  --query 'GroupId' \
  --output text)

# Allow SSH access
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $SG_ID \
  --protocol tcp \
  --port 22 \
  --cidr 0.0.0.0/0 \
  --region us-east-1

# Allow HTTP and HTTPS
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $SG_ID \
  --protocol tcp \
  --port 80 \
  --cidr 0.0.0.0/0 \
  --region us-east-1

aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $SG_ID \
  --protocol tcp \
  --port 443 \
  --cidr 0.0.0.0/0 \
  --region us-east-1

# Allow Django development server (8000)
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $SG_ID \
  --protocol tcp \
  --port 8000 \
  --cidr 0.0.0.0/0 \
  --region us-east-1

# Launch spot instance
aws ec2 request-spot-instances \
  --spot-price "0.05" \
  --instance-count 1 \
  --type "one-time" \
  --launch-specification '{
    "ImageId":"ami-0c55b159cbfafe1f0",
    "InstanceType":"t2.small",
    "KeyName":"anihpj-dev-key",
    "SecurityGroupIds":["'$SG_ID'"],
    "SubnetId":"'$SUBNET_ID'",
    "Monitoring":{"Enabled":true},
    "TagSpecifications":[{
      "ResourceType":"instance",
      "Tags":[
        {"Key":"Name","Value":"anihpj-jobpost-spot"},
        {"Key":"App","Value":"jobpost"},
        {"Key":"Type","Value":"spot"}
      ]
    }]
  }' \
  --region us-east-1
{ "SpotInstanceRequests": [ { "SpotInstanceRequestId": "sir-0abc123def456", "State": "open", "Status": { "Code": "pending-evaluation", "Message": "Your Spot request is being evaluated." }, "LaunchSpecification": { "ImageId": "ami-0c55b159cbfafe1f0", "InstanceType": "t2.small", "KeyName": "anihpj-dev-key", "SecurityGroups": [ { "GroupId": "sg-0123456789abcdef0" } ] }, "CreateTime": "2025-01-11T14:52:10.000Z", "Tags": [ { "Key": "Name", "Value": "anihpj-jobpost-spot" }, { "Key": "App", "Value": "jobpost" } ] } ] } # Spot request processing output: # # SpotInstanceRequest Status: # ID: sir-0abc123def456 # State: open (request submitted) # Status: pending-evaluation (AWS evaluating availability) # Price: $0.05/hour (vs on-demand ~$0.23/hour) # # VPC and Networking created: # VPC CIDR: 10.0.0.0/16 # Subnet: 10.0.1.0/24 in us-east-1a # Security Groups configured for SSH (22), HTTP (80), HTTPS (443), Django (8000)
# Spot Instance Django Environment Setup from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost from django.conf import settings # Spot instance configuration (cost-optimized) spot_config = { 'spot_request_id': 'sir-0abc123def456', 'instance_type': 't2.small', 'price_per_hour': 0.05, 'cost_vs_ondemand': 'Saves ~$0.18/hour (78% cheaper)', 'expected_monthly_cost': 36.50, # ~150 hours/month 'availability': 'May be interrupted by AWS' } # VPC and networking configuration vpc_config = { 'vpc_id': '10.0.0.0/16', 'subnet': '10.0.1.0/24', 'availability_zone': 'us-east-1a', 'security_groups': { 'ssh': 'port 22 (0.0.0.0/0)', 'http': 'port 80 (0.0.0.0/0)', 'https': 'port 443 (0.0.0.0/0)', 'django_dev': 'port 8000 (0.0.0.0/0)' } } # Django application configuration for spot instance # Once instance is running, these models will be available: Skills.objects.all() # Skills model ready # Output: Author.objects.select_related('user', 'location').all() # Authors with relationships # Output: Location.objects.all() # Job locations # Output: JobPost.objects.filter(author__isnull=False).count() # Valid job postings # Output: 0 # Cost tracking query (add to models if needed) cost_tracking = { 'instance_type': 't2.small', 'launch_time': '2025-01-11T14:52:10.000Z', 'hourly_cost': 0.05, 'monthly_estimate': 36.50, 'django_apps': ['jobpost'], 'models': ['Skills', 'User', 'Author', 'Location', 'JobPost'] }

describe-instances

Retrieves detailed information about EC2 instances. Shows status, IP addresses, security groups, and other configuration details for managing your Django application instances. Essential for monitoring, debugging, and managing your jobpost application deployment.

Syntax
aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids {instance-id} \
  --filters "Name=tag:Name,Values={tag-value}" \
  --query 'Reservations[*].Instances[*].[InstanceId,State.Name,PublicIpAddress,PrivateIpAddress,InstanceType]' \
  --output table
Parameters Description
  • --instance-ids (list): Specific instance IDs to describe. Optional - if omitted, returns all instances. Example: i-0987654321fedcba0
  • --filters (list): Filter instances by various criteria. Common filters: instance-state-name (running, stopped, terminated), tag:Name (tag value), vpc-id, subnet-id, security-group-id
  • --query (string): JMESPath query to extract specific fields from output. Example: 'Reservations[*].Instances[*].[InstanceId,State.Name]'
  • --output (string): Output format - text, json, table. Recommended: json for parsing, table for viewing
  • --max-results (integer): Maximum number of results to return (1-1000). Default: all instances
  • --next-token (string): Token for pagination when results exceed max-results
Return Value
  • Reservations (Array): Container for instances grouped by reservation
  • Instances (Array): List of EC2 instances with details
  • InstanceId (string): Unique identifier for the instance
  • State (Object): Current state (pending, running, stopping, stopped, shutting-down, terminated)
  • PublicIpAddress (string): Public IP address (if assigned)
  • PrivateIpAddress (string): Private IP within VPC
  • Tags (Array): Key-value pairs for organizing instances
5 Detailed EC2 describe-instances Examples

Example 5: List Stopped Instances and Plan Recovery

Find all stopped instances for the jobpost application and gather information needed to restart them and verify data integrity.

#!/bin/bash
# Find all stopped jobpost instances
aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --filters "Name=tag:App,Values=jobpost" \
             "Name=instance-state-name,Values=stopped" \
  --query 'Reservations[*].Instances[*].[InstanceId,InstanceType,State.Name,PublicIpAddress,PrivateIpAddress,StateTransitionReason,Tags[?Key==`Name`].Value|[0]]' \
  --output table \
  --region us-east-1

# Get cost savings from stopped instances
STOPPED_COUNT=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --filters "Name=tag:App,Values=jobpost" \
             "Name=instance-state-name,Values=stopped" \
  --query 'length(Reservations[*].Instances[*][])' \
  --output text)

# Estimate savings (t3.small costs ~$0.0376/hour, stopped = free)
MONTHLY_SAVINGS=$(echo "scale=2; $STOPPED_COUNT * 30 * 24 * 0.0376" | bc)

echo "Stopped instances: $STOPPED_COUNT"
echo "Estimated monthly storage cost: $MONTHLY_SAVINGS (storage only, compute is $0)"

# Show detailed info for restart planning
aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --filters "Name=tag:App,Values=jobpost" \
             "Name=instance-state-name,Values=stopped" \
  --query 'Reservations[*].Instances[*].[InstanceId,InstanceType,StateTransitionReason,Tags]' \
  --output json > stopped-instances-recovery.json

start-instances

Starts one or more stopped EC2 instances. Useful for resuming suspended Django application instances without terminating them. Restores the instance to running state and resumes billing for compute time.

Syntax
aws ec2 start-instances \
  --instance-ids {instance-id} \
  --region {region}
Parameters Description
  • --instance-ids (list, required): One or more instance IDs to start. Example: i-0987654321fedcba0. Can accept multiple IDs separated by spaces
  • --region (string): AWS region where instances are located. Example: us-east-1, eu-west-1
  • --additional-info (string): Additional information about the start request (rarely used)
Return Value
  • StartingInstances (Array): List of instances being started
  • InstanceId (string): ID of the instance
  • CurrentState (Object): State transitioning to running
  • PreviousState (Object): State before start (was stopped)
5 Detailed EC2 start-instances Examples

Example 2: Start Multiple Backup Instances Simultaneously

Resume multiple stopped backup instances to create a failover cluster for the jobpost application.

#!/bin/bash
# Start multiple backup instances at once
INSTANCE_IDS="i-0def1abc2ghi3jk4 i-0ghi1def2abc3jk4"

aws ec2 start-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_IDS \
  --region us-east-1

echo "Starting instances: $INSTANCE_IDS"

# Wait for all instances to be running
for instance_id in $INSTANCE_IDS; do
  echo "Waiting for $instance_id to start..."
  aws ec2 wait instance-running \
    --instance-ids $instance_id \
    --region us-east-1
  echo "✓ $instance_id is running"
done

# Display startup summary
aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_IDS \
  --query 'Reservations[*].Instances[*].[InstanceId,State.Name,PublicIpAddress,LaunchTime]' \
  --output table \
  --region us-east-1
{ "StartingInstances": [ { "InstanceId": "i-0def1abc2ghi3jk4", "CurrentState": { "Code": 0, "Name": "pending" }, "PreviousState": { "Code": 80, "Name": "stopped" } }, { "InstanceId": "i-0ghi1def2abc3jk4", "CurrentState": { "Code": 0, "Name": "pending" }, "PreviousState": { "Code": 80, "Name": "stopped" } } ] } Starting instances: i-0def1abc2ghi3jk4 i-0ghi1def2abc3jk4 Waiting for i-0def1abc2ghi3jk4 to start... ✓ i-0def1abc2ghi3jk4 is running Waiting for i-0ghi1def2abc3jk4 to start... ✓ i-0ghi1def2abc3jk4 is running INSTANCEID | STATE | PUBLICIPADDRESS | LAUNCHTIME i-0def1abc2ghi3jk4 | running | 54.234.123.45 | 2025-01-10T13:45:30Z i-0ghi1def2abc3jk4 | running | 54.245.234.56 | 2025-01-09T09:22:15Z
# Backup cluster startup and data synchronization from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost from django.db import connections from django.db.models import Count import asyncio # Backup instances being started backup_instances = [ {'id': 'i-0def1abc2ghi3jk4', 'ip': '54.234.123.45', 'name': 'backup-1'}, {'id': 'i-0ghi1def2abc3jk4', 'ip': '54.245.234.56', 'name': 'backup-2'} ] print(f"Starting {len(backup_instances)} backup instances for jobpost app...") # Output: Starting 2 backup instances for jobpost app... # After startup, verify data replication for backup in backup_instances: print(f"\nVerifying {backup['name']} ({backup['ip']}):") # Check model counts to verify replication skills_count = Skills.objects.count() authors_count = Author.objects.count() jobs_count = JobPost.objects.count() print(f" Skills replicated: {skills_count}") # Output: Skills replicated: 0 print(f" Authors replicated: {authors_count}") # Output: Authors replicated: 0 print(f" Jobs replicated: {jobs_count}") # Output: Jobs replicated: 0 # Cluster status after startup cluster_status = { 'total_backup_nodes': len(backup_instances), 'expected_data_consistency': True, 'replication_lag_seconds': 0, 'models_synced': ['Skills', 'User', 'Author', 'Location', 'JobPost'] } print(f"\nBackup cluster status:") print(f" Total nodes: {cluster_status['total_backup_nodes']}") print(f" Data consistent: {cluster_status['expected_data_consistency']}") print(f" Models synced: {', '.join(cluster_status['models_synced'])}")
Example 3: Start Instances and Update DNS Records

Resume stopped production instances and automatically update Route 53 DNS to point to new IP addresses.

#!/bin/bash
# Start production instances and update DNS
PROD_INSTANCES="i-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8 i-0abc1def2ghi3jk4"
HOSTED_ZONE_ID="Z1234567890ABC"
DOMAIN="jobpost-api.example.com"

# Start instances
aws ec2 start-instances \
  --instance-ids $PROD_INSTANCES \
  --region us-east-1

# Wait for startup
for id in $PROD_INSTANCES; do
  aws ec2 wait instance-running --instance-ids $id --region us-east-1
done

# Get new public IPs
PUBLIC_IPS=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $PROD_INSTANCES \
  --query 'Reservations[*].Instances[*].PublicIpAddress' \
  --output text \
  --region us-east-1)

# Update DNS records
echo "Instances restarted. Public IPs: $PUBLIC_IPS"
echo "DNS records would be updated with new IPs"

# Verify instances are ready
aws ec2 describe-instance-status \
  --instance-ids $PROD_INSTANCES \
  --query 'InstanceStatuses[*].[InstanceId,InstanceStatus.Status,SystemStatus.Status]' \
  --output table \
  --region us-east-1

Example 4: Start Instance with Dependency Check (Database and Cache)

Resume an application instance and verify all dependent services (database, cache, API endpoints) are ready before routing traffic.

#!/bin/bash
# Start instance with health verification
INSTANCE_ID="i-0987654321fedcba0"
MAX_RETRIES=30
RETRY_INTERVAL=5

# Start the instance
echo "Starting instance $INSTANCE_ID..."
aws ec2 start-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

# Wait for instance to be running
aws ec2 wait instance-running \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

# Get IP address
PUBLIC_IP=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].PublicIpAddress' \
  --output text \
  --region us-east-1)

echo "Instance $INSTANCE_ID is running at $PUBLIC_IP"

# Check Django app availability
echo "Checking Django app health..."
for ((i=1; i<=MAX_RETRIES; i++)); do
  HTTP_CODE=$(curl -s -o /dev/null -w "%{http_code}" http://$PUBLIC_IP:8000/health || echo "000")
  
  if [ "$HTTP_CODE" = "200" ]; then
    echo "✓ Django app is healthy (HTTP $HTTP_CODE)"
    break
  else
    echo "  Attempt $i/$MAX_RETRIES - HTTP $HTTP_CODE (waiting...)"
    sleep $RETRY_INTERVAL
  fi
done

echo "Instance startup complete and verified"

Example 5: Start Instances with Monitoring and CloudWatch Alarms

Resume instances and enable detailed monitoring with CloudWatch alarms to track CPU, memory, and disk usage.

#!/bin/bash
# Start instances with monitoring enabled
INSTANCE_IDS="i-0abc1def2ghi3jk4 i-0xyz9abc8def7ghi"

# Start instances
aws ec2 start-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_IDS \
  --region us-east-1

# Enable detailed monitoring (1-minute intervals instead of 5-minute)
for instance_id in $INSTANCE_IDS; do
  aws ec2 monitor-instances \
    --instance-ids $instance_id \
    --region us-east-1
done

echo "✓ Detailed monitoring enabled"

# Create CloudWatch alarms for CPU
for instance_id in $INSTANCE_IDS; do
  aws cloudwatch put-metric-alarm \
    --alarm-name "jobpost-high-cpu-$instance_id" \
    --alarm-description "Alert when CPU exceeds 80%" \
    --metric-name CPUUtilization \
    --namespace AWS/EC2 \
    --statistic Average \
    --period 300 \
    --threshold 80 \
    --comparison-operator GreaterThanThreshold \
    --dimensions Name=InstanceId,Value=$instance_id \
    --evaluation-periods 2 \
    --alarm-actions arn:aws:sns:us-east-1:123456789012:jobpost-alerts \
    --region us-east-1
done

echo "✓ CloudWatch alarms created"

# Wait for instances to be fully running
for instance_id in $INSTANCE_IDS; do
  aws ec2 wait instance-running --instance-ids $instance_id --region us-east-1
done

# Display monitoring status
aws cloudwatch list-metrics \
  --namespace AWS/EC2 \
  --metric-name CPUUtilization \
  --query 'Metrics[?Dimensions[?Name==`InstanceId`]]' \
  --output json \
  --region us-east-1

stop-instances

Stops one or more running EC2 instances. Preserves the instance for later restart while stopping charges for compute time (only storage charges apply). Data and configuration remain intact on the instance.

Syntax
aws ec2 stop-instances \
  --instance-ids {instance-id} \
  --force \
  --region {region}
Parameters Description
  • --instance-ids (list, required): One or more instance IDs to stop. Multiple IDs can be provided separated by spaces
  • --force (boolean): Forces shutdown without graceful stop. Use only when graceful stop is not responding. Can cause data loss - use with caution
  • --region (string): AWS region where instances are located
  • --hibernate (boolean): Hibernates the instance instead of shutting down (requires EBS-backed instance with hibernation enabled)
Return Value
  • StoppingInstances (Array): List of instances being stopped
  • InstanceId (string): ID of the instance
  • CurrentState (Object): State transitioning to stopped
  • PreviousState (Object): State before stop (was running)
5 Detailed EC2 stop-instances Examples
Example 1: Stop Development Instance for Maintenance

Gracefully stop a development instance to perform system updates and maintenance on the jobpost application server.

#!/bin/bash
# Stop development instance gracefully
INSTANCE_ID="i-0987654321fedcba0"

echo "Stopping development instance: $INSTANCE_ID"

# Stop the instance (graceful shutdown)
aws ec2 stop-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

# Wait for instance to be stopped
aws ec2 wait instance-stopped \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

# Verify it's stopped
FINAL_STATE=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].State.Name' \
  --output text \
  --region us-east-1)

echo "Instance $INSTANCE_ID is now: $FINAL_STATE"
echo "Instance charges paused - only storage costs $0.10/month"
{ "StoppingInstances": [ { "InstanceId": "i-0987654321fedcba0", "CurrentState": { "Code": 64, "Name": "stopping" }, "PreviousState": { "Code": 16, "Name": "running" } } ] } Instance i-0987654321fedcba0 is now: stopped Instance charges paused - only storage costs $0.10/month

Example 2: Stop Multiple Backup Instances to Reduce Costs

Stop multiple backup instances during off-peak hours or when not needed to reduce AWS costs while keeping them available for quick restart.

#!/bin/bash
# Stop multiple backup instances for cost optimization
BACKUP_INSTANCES="i-0def1abc2ghi3jk4 i-0ghi1def2abc3jk4"

echo "Stopping backup instances: $BACKUP_INSTANCES"

# Stop all instances
aws ec2 stop-instances \
  --instance-ids $BACKUP_INSTANCES \
  --region us-east-1

# Wait for all to be stopped
for instance_id in $BACKUP_INSTANCES; do
  echo "Waiting for $instance_id..."
  aws ec2 wait instance-stopped \
    --instance-ids $instance_id \
    --region us-east-1
  echo "✓ $instance_id stopped"
done

# Calculate cost savings
INSTANCE_COUNT=$(echo $BACKUP_INSTANCES | wc -w)
HOURLY_RATE=0.0376  # t3.small hourly cost
HOURS_PER_MONTH=730

SAVINGS=$(echo "scale=2; $INSTANCE_COUNT * $HOURLY_RATE * $HOURS_PER_MONTH" | bc)

echo ""
echo "Cost Analysis:"
echo "  Stopped instances: $INSTANCE_COUNT"
echo "  Hourly rate per instance: \$$HOURLY_RATE"
echo "  Monthly savings: \$$SAVINGS (compute only)"
echo "  Storage cost remaining: \$0.10/instance/month"

Cost breakdown cost_analysis = { 'monthly_compute_savings': backup_shutdown['estimated_monthly_savings'], 'monthly_storage_cost': 0.20, # 2 instances × $0.10 'net_monthly_savings': backup_shutdown['estimated_monthly_savings'] - 0.20, 'annual_savings': (backup_shutdown['estimated_monthly_savings'] - 0.20) * 12 } print(f"\nCost analysis:") print(f" Monthly compute savings: ${cost_analysis['monthly_compute_savings']}") print(f" Monthly storage cost: ${cost_analysis['monthly_storage_cost']}") print(f" Net monthly savings: ${cost_analysis['net_monthly_savings']:.2f}") print(f" Annual savings: ${cost_analysis['annual_savings']:.2f}")
Example 3: Stop Instance with Pre-Stop Data Export

Before stopping a production instance, export jobpost database snapshot and create backup for disaster recovery.

#!/bin/bash
# Export data before stopping instance
INSTANCE_ID="i-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
BACKUP_BUCKET="s3://anihpj-backups"
TIMESTAMP=$(date +%Y%m%d-%H%M%S)

echo "Pre-stop backup: exporting jobpost data..."

# Create database dump (SSH into instance and run)
# aws ssm send-command \
#   --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
#   --document-name "AWS-RunShellScript" \
#   --parameters 'commands=[
#     "pg_dump -U postgres jobpost_db > /tmp/jobpost-backup-$TIMESTAMP.sql",
#     "tar -czf /tmp/jobpost-backup-$TIMESTAMP.tar.gz -C /var/www anihpj/",
#     "aws s3 cp /tmp/jobpost-backup-$TIMESTAMP.sql $BACKUP_BUCKET/",
#     "aws s3 cp /tmp/jobpost-backup-$TIMESTAMP.tar.gz $BACKUP_BUCKET/"
#   ]' \
#   --region us-east-1

# For demonstration, show what would be backed up
echo "Backup items for instance $INSTANCE_ID:"
echo "  - PostgreSQL database: jobpost_db"
echo "  - Django application: /var/www/anihpj/"
echo "  - Static files: /var/www/anihpj/staticfiles/"
echo "  - Media files: /var/www/anihpj/media/"

# Create EBS snapshot of instance volume
aws ec2 create-snapshot \
  --volume-id vol-0123456789abcdef0 \
  --description "Pre-stop backup of jobpost instance $INSTANCE_ID - $TIMESTAMP" \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=snapshot,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=jobpost-backup-$TIMESTAMP},{Key=Instance,Value=$INSTANCE_ID}]" \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ EBS snapshot created"

# Now stop the instance
echo ""
echo "Stopping instance $INSTANCE_ID..."
aws ec2 stop-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

aws ec2 wait instance-stopped \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Instance stopped - backups secured"

Example 4: Stop Production Instance Gracefully with Load Balancer Deregistration

Remove a production instance from load balancer before stopping to ensure no traffic loss during maintenance window.

#!/bin/bash
# Graceful production instance stop with LB deregistration
INSTANCE_ID="i-0abc1def2ghi3jk4"
TARGET_GROUP_ARN="arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:us-east-1:123456789012:targetgroup/jobpost-api/abc123def456"
DRAINING_TIMEOUT=300  # 5 minutes

echo "Gracefully stopping production instance: $INSTANCE_ID"
echo "Step 1: Deregister from load balancer..."

# Get current instance details
INSTANCE_PORT=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].SecurityGroups[0].GroupId' \
  --output text)

# Deregister from target group
aws elbv2 deregister-targets \
  --target-group-arn $TARGET_GROUP_ARN \
  --targets Id=$INSTANCE_ID,Port=8000 \
  --region us-east-1

echo "  ✓ Instance deregistered from load balancer"
echo "Step 2: Waiting for connection draining ($DRAINING_TIMEOUT seconds)..."

# Wait for existing connections to close
sleep $DRAINING_TIMEOUT

echo "  ✓ Connection draining complete"
echo "Step 3: Stopping instance..."

# Stop the instance
aws ec2 stop-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

# Verify it's stopping
aws ec2 wait instance-stopped \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "  ✓ Instance stopped successfully"
echo ""
echo "Maintenance complete. Instance ready for updates."
echo "To resume: aws ec2 start-instances --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID"

Instance ready for updates. To resume: aws ec2 start-instances --instance-ids i-0abc1def2ghi3jk4
# Production instance graceful shutdown with LB deregistration from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost from django.db.models import Q from django.utils import timezone import logging # Configure logging logger = logging.getLogger(__name__) # Production shutdown context production_stop = { 'instance_id': 'i-0abc1def2ghi3jk4', 'load_balancer_target_group': 'jobpost-api', 'draining_timeout_seconds': 300, 'maintenance_reason': 'Security patches and updates' } print(f"Production shutdown sequence initiated") print(f"Instance: {production_stop['instance_id']}") # Step 1: Log current active sessions active_sessions = { 'timestamp': timezone.now().isoformat(), 'instance_id': production_stop['instance_id'], 'active_jobs': JobPost.objects.filter(status='published').count(), 'active_authors': Author.objects.filter(user__is_active=True).count() } print(f"\nActive traffic snapshot:") print(f" Published jobs: {active_sessions['active_jobs']}") # Step 3: Prepare for maintenance maintenance_tasks = [ 'Apply security patches', 'Update Django dependencies', 'Optimize database indexes', 'Review and clear logs', 'Test jobpost app endpoints' ] print(f"\nScheduled maintenance:") for i, task in enumerate(maintenance_tasks, 1): print(f" {i}. {task}") # Final state shutdown_complete = { 'instance_id': production_stop['instance_id'], 'state': 'stopped', 'data_status': 'preserved', 'ready_for_restart': True, 'estimated_maintenance_time': '30 minutes' } print(f"\n✓ Instance safe to stop") print(f"✓ No active connections") print(f"✓ Data preserved on EBS") print(f"✓ Ready for: {shutdown_complete['estimated_maintenance_time']} maintenance")
Example 5: Stop Instance with Scheduled Restart

Stop instance and schedule automatic restart using AWS Systems Manager for predictable downtime and patching windows.

#!/bin/bash
# Stop instance and schedule automatic restart
INSTANCE_ID="i-0xyz9abc8def7ghi"
RESTART_TIME="2025-01-12T02:00:00Z"  # 2 AM UTC tomorrow

echo "Scheduling maintenance window for instance: $INSTANCE_ID"

# Stop the instance
aws ec2 stop-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

# Wait for it to stop
aws ec2 wait instance-stopped \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Instance stopped"

# Schedule restart using SSM Automation (pseudo-code)
# In practice, you'd use EventBridge or Lambda for this
cat > restart-schedule.json << EOF
{
  "instance_id": "$INSTANCE_ID",
  "scheduled_restart_time": "$RESTART_TIME",
  "automation_document": "AWS-StartEC2Instance",
  "tags": {
    "Maintenance": "scheduled",
    "App": "jobpost"
  }
}
EOF

echo "✓ Maintenance window scheduled"
echo "  Instance: $INSTANCE_ID"
echo "  Restart time: $RESTART_TIME"
echo "  Status: Stopped and waiting for automatic restart"

# Display status
aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].[InstanceId,State.Name,LaunchTime]' \
  --output table \
  --region us-east-1

terminate-instances

Terminates (permanently deletes) one or more EC2 instances. This is irreversible - the instance and its data will be destroyed. Use with extreme caution, especially for production instances. Attached EBS volumes marked for deletion will be removed.

Syntax
aws ec2 terminate-instances \
  --instance-ids {instance-id} \
  --region {region}
Parameters Description
  • --instance-ids (list, required): One or more instance IDs to terminate. Cannot be undone. Multiple IDs separated by spaces
  • --region (string): AWS region where instances are located
  • --dry-run (boolean): Checks whether you have the required permissions without actually terminating
Return Value
  • TerminatingInstances (Array): List of instances being terminated
  • InstanceId (string): ID of the instance
  • CurrentState (Object): State transitioning to terminated
  • PreviousState (Object): State before termination
5 Detailed EC2 terminate-instances Examples
Example 1: Terminate Development Instance After Testing Complete

Remove a temporary development instance after testing cycle is complete to reduce unnecessary costs. Always backup data first!

#!/bin/bash
# Terminate development instance after testing
INSTANCE_ID="i-0987654321fedcba0"

echo "⚠️  WARNING: Terminating instance will PERMANENTLY DELETE all data!"
echo "Instance ID: $INSTANCE_ID"

# Safety check - require confirmation
read -p "Are you sure you want to terminate? Type 'yes' to confirm: " CONFIRM

if [ "$CONFIRM" != "yes" ]; then
  echo "Termination cancelled."
  exit 0
fi

echo "Creating final snapshot before termination..."

# Get the volume ID
VOLUME_ID=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].BlockDeviceMappings[0].Ebs.VolumeId' \
  --output text \
  --region us-east-1)

# Create snapshot as final backup
aws ec2 create-snapshot \
  --volume-id $VOLUME_ID \
  --description "Final backup before termination of $INSTANCE_ID" \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Final snapshot created: $VOLUME_ID"

# Terminate the instance
echo ""
echo "Terminating instance $INSTANCE_ID..."
aws ec2 terminate-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Instance termination initiated"
echo "  State: shutting-down → terminated"
echo "  Completion time: ~30 seconds"

Type 'yes' to confirm: yes Creating final snapshot before termination... { "Snapshot": { "SnapshotId": "snap-final0987654321", "VolumeId": "vol-0123456789abcdef0", "State": "pending", "StartTime": "2025-01-11T16:00:00.000Z", "Description": "Final backup before termination of i-0987654321fedcba0" } } ✓ Final snapshot created: vol-0123456789abcdef0 Terminating instance i-0987654321fedcba0... { "TerminatingInstances": [{ "InstanceId": "i-0987654321fedcba0", "CurrentState": { "Code": 32, "Name": "shutting-down" }, "PreviousState": { "Code": 80, "Name": "stopped" } }] } ✓ Instance termination initiated State: shutting-down → terminated Completion time: ~30 seconds

Example 2: Terminate Multiple Failed Instances After Retry Attempts

Remove multiple instances that failed health checks and cleanup procedures to avoid unnecessary charges and resource waste.

#!/bin/bash
# Terminate failed instances
FAILED_INSTANCES="i-0def1abc2ghi3jk4 i-0ghi1def2abc3jk4"
FAILURE_REASON="Health check failures - beyond recovery"

echo "Cleaning up failed instances..."
echo "Reason: $FAILURE_REASON"
echo ""

# Check each instance before termination
for instance_id in $FAILED_INSTANCES; do
  echo "Instance $instance_id details:"
  
  # Get status
  STATUS=$(aws ec2 describe-instance-status \
    --instance-ids $instance_id \
    --query 'InstanceStatuses[0].InstanceStatus.Status' \
    --output text \
    --region us-east-1 2>/dev/null || echo "N/A")
  
  echo "  Status: $STATUS"
  echo "  Action: Will be terminated"
done

echo ""
echo "Proceeding with termination of $FAILED_INSTANCES..."

# Terminate all failed instances
aws ec2 terminate-instances \
  --instance-ids $FAILED_INSTANCES \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Termination initiated for failed instances"

# Calculate cost savings
INSTANCE_COUNT=$(echo $FAILED_INSTANCES | wc -w)
HOURLY_RATE=0.0376  # t3.small
DAILY_SAVINGS=$(echo "scale=2; $INSTANCE_COUNT * $HOURLY_RATE * 24" | bc)

echo ""
echo "Cost savings from termination:"
echo "  Failed instances removed: $INSTANCE_COUNT"
echo "  Daily savings: \$$DAILY_SAVINGS"
echo "  Estimated monthly savings: \$$(echo "scale=2; $DAILY_SAVINGS * 30" | bc)"

# Failed instances cleanup and recovery from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost from django.db import connections, connection from django.core.management import call_command # Failed instances being terminated failed_instances = [ {'id': 'i-0def1abc2ghi3jk4', 'status': 'impaired'}, {'id': 'i-0ghi1def2abc3jk4', 'status': 'impaired'} ] print(f"Terminating {len(failed_instances)} failed instances") # Verify all data is on healthy primary instance print(f"\nVerifying data on primary instance...") try: primary_data_count = (Skills.objects.count() + Author.objects.count() + JobPost.objects.count() + Location.objects.count()) print(f"✓ Primary has {primary_data_count} records") # Output: Primary has 0 records except Exception as e: print(f"✗ Primary access error: {e}") # Cleanup impact analysis cleanup_summary = { 'instances_removed': len(failed_instances), 'data_loss': 'None - replicated on primary', 'monthly_savings': 54.00, 'failover_impact': 'Backup capacity removed' } print(f"\nCleanup Summary:") print(f" Instances removed: {cleanup_summary['instances_removed']}") print(f" Data safety: {cleanup_summary['data_loss']}") print(f" Monthly savings: ${cleanup_summary['monthly_savings']}") print(f"\n✓ Failed instances terminated") print(f"✓ Primary instance still healthy")

#!/bin/bash

Example 4: Terminate Instance with Pre-Termination Health Report

Generate comprehensive health and performance report before terminating instance for post-mortem analysis.

#!/bin/bash
# Generate health report before termination
INSTANCE_ID="i-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
REPORT_BUCKET="s3://anihpj-reports"
TIMESTAMP=$(date +%Y%m%d-%H%M%S)

echo "Generating pre-termination health report for $INSTANCE_ID..."

# Get comprehensive instance details
aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0]' \
  --output json > report-$INSTANCE_ID-$TIMESTAMP.json

# Get CloudWatch metrics summary (last 7 days)
echo "Collecting CloudWatch metrics..."
aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
  --namespace AWS/EC2 \
  --metric-name CPUUtilization \
  --dimensions Name=InstanceId,Value=$INSTANCE_ID \
  --start-time $(date -u -d '7 days ago' +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S) \
  --end-time $(date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S) \
  --period 3600 \
  --statistics Average Maximum \
  --output json > metrics-$INSTANCE_ID-$TIMESTAMP.json

# Upload reports
aws s3 cp report-$INSTANCE_ID-$TIMESTAMP.json $REPORT_BUCKET/pre-termination-reports/
aws s3 cp metrics-$INSTANCE_ID-$TIMESTAMP.json $REPORT_BUCKET/pre-termination-reports/

echo "✓ Health report generated: report-$INSTANCE_ID-$TIMESTAMP.json"
echo "✓ Metrics saved: metrics-$INSTANCE_ID-$TIMESTAMP.json"
echo "✓ Reports uploaded to S3"

echo ""
echo "Final metrics summary:"
echo "  CPU Utilization (last 7 days): Check CloudWatch"
echo "  Network In/Out: Check CloudWatch"
echo "  Disk I/O: Check CloudWatch"

# Now safe to terminate
echo ""
echo "Proceeding with termination..."
aws ec2 terminate-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Instance $INSTANCE_ID terminated"
echo "✓ Health reports available in S3 for post-mortem analysis"

Example 5: Terminate Instance with Rollback Safety - Snapshot Retention

Safely terminate instance while preserving EBS snapshots for potential rollback if issues are discovered post-termination.

#!/bin/bash
# Terminate with snapshot retention for safety
INSTANCE_ID="i-0lmn5opq6rst7uvw"
RETENTION_DAYS=30

echo "Safe termination with snapshot retention"
echo "Instance: $INSTANCE_ID"
echo "Snapshot retention: $RETENTION_DAYS days"

# Get all volumes attached to this instance
VOLUME_IDS=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].BlockDeviceMappings[*].Ebs.VolumeId' \
  --output text \
  --region us-east-1)

echo ""
echo "Creating final snapshots for rollback safety..."

# Create snapshots of all volumes
for volume_id in $VOLUME_IDS; do
  SNAPSHOT=$(aws ec2 create-snapshot \
    --volume-id $volume_id \
    --description "Rollback snapshot for terminated instance $INSTANCE_ID - Retain $RETENTION_DAYS days" \
    --tag-specifications "ResourceType=snapshot,Tags=[{Key=Retention,Value=$RETENTION_DAYS-days},{Key=OriginalInstance,Value=$INSTANCE_ID},{Key=RollbackSafe,Value=true}]" \
    --region us-east-1 \
    --query 'SnapshotId' \
    --output text)
  
  echo "  ✓ Snapshot created: $SNAPSHOT (Volume: $volume_id)"
done

echo ""
echo "Terminating instance $INSTANCE_ID..."

# Terminate the instance but keep snapshots
aws ec2 terminate-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Instance terminated"
echo ""
echo "Safety measures in place:"
echo "  - EBS snapshots retained for $RETENTION_DAYS days"
echo "  - Snapshots can be used to recover data or create new instances"
echo "  - Snapshots will auto-expire after $RETENTION_DAYS days (cost-saving)"
echo "  - Tags applied: RollbackSafe=true for easy identification"

reboot-instances

Reboots one or more EC2 instances. The instance reboots without stopping - no data loss but brief downtime (1-2 minutes). Useful for applying system patches, clearing kernel issues, or refreshing the OS without terminating the instance.

Syntax
aws ec2 reboot-instances \
  --instance-ids {instance-id} \
  --region {region}
Parameters Description
  • --instance-ids (list, required): One or more instance IDs to reboot. Instances must be in running state
  • --region (string): AWS region where instances are located
  • --dry-run (boolean): Checks permissions without actually rebooting
Return Value
  • Return (boolean): True if reboot request accepted
  • ResponseMetadata (Object): HTTP response metadata and request ID
5 Detailed EC2 reboot-instances Examples
Example 1: Reboot Development Instance for Testing Fresh OS State

Reboot development instance to verify application behavior on clean OS boot and test initialization scripts.

#!/bin/bash
# Reboot dev instance for fresh OS state testing
INSTANCE_ID="i-0987654321fedcba0"
APP_USER="ubuntu"

echo "Rebooting dev instance for fresh state testing..."
echo "Instance: $INSTANCE_ID"

# Verify instance is running
STATUS=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].State.Name' \
  --output text \
  --region us-east-1)

if [ "$STATUS" != "running" ]; then
  echo "✗ Instance is not running (status: $STATUS)"
  exit 1
fi

echo "✓ Instance is running - proceeding with reboot"
echo ""

# Initiate reboot
aws ec2 reboot-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Reboot initiated for $INSTANCE_ID"
echo "  Reboot time: 2-3 minutes"
echo "  Data preserved: YES"

# Wait for instance to come back online
echo ""
echo "Waiting for instance to restart and reach running status..."

aws ec2 wait instance-running \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Instance is running again after reboot"

# Verify system is responsive
sleep 30  # Wait for services to start
IP=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].PrivateIpAddress' \
  --output text \
  --region us-east-1)

echo ""
echo "Post-reboot verification:"
echo "  Instance IP: $IP"
echo "  Boot logs available via EC2 Instance Connect or SSM"
echo "  Application initialization: Check systemd journal"

Example 2: Reboot Production Instance During Maintenance Window

Safely reboot production instance within planned maintenance window with health checks and load balancer management.

#!/bin/bash
# Reboot production instance during maintenance window
INSTANCE_ID="i-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
ALB_TARGET_GROUP="arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:us-east-1:123456789012:targetgroup/django-app/abc123"
MAINTENANCE_WINDOW="2025-01-15T02:00-06:00"  # Off-peak hours

echo "Production Instance Reboot - Maintenance Window"
echo "Instance: $INSTANCE_ID"
echo "Maintenance window: $MAINTENANCE_WINDOW"
echo "Expected downtime: 2-3 minutes"

# Pre-reboot health check
echo ""
echo "Pre-reboot checks:"
aws ec2 describe-instance-status \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --query 'InstanceStatuses[0].[SystemStatus.Status, InstanceStatus.Status]' \
  --output text \
  --region us-east-1

# Deregister from load balancer before reboot
echo ""
echo "Deregistering from ALB target group..."
aws elbv2 deregister-targets \
  --target-group-arn $ALB_TARGET_GROUP \
  --targets Id=$INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Deregistered from load balancer"

# Wait for connection draining
echo "Waiting for connection draining (30 seconds)..."
sleep 30

# Perform the reboot
echo ""
echo "Initiating reboot..."
aws ec2 reboot-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Reboot initiated"
echo "  System rebooting... (2-3 minutes)"

# Wait for instance to fully restart
aws ec2 wait instance-status-ok \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Instance fully started and healthy"

# Re-register with load balancer
echo ""
echo "Re-registering with ALB target group..."
aws elbv2 register-targets \
  --target-group-arn $ALB_TARGET_GROUP \
  --targets Id=$INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Re-registered with load balancer"
echo ""
echo "Instance is now serving traffic again"

Initiating reboot... ✓ Reboot initiated System rebooting... (2-3 minutes) ✓ Instance fully started and healthy Re-registering with ALB target group... ✓ Re-registered with load balancer Instance is now serving traffic again

wait for active requests to complete active_connections = { 'active_requests': 24, 'drain_timeout': 30, 'connections_completed': 22, 'new_requests_blocked': True } print(f"\nConnection draining:") print(f" Active requests being completed: {active_connections['active_requests']}") print(f" Drain timeout: {active_connections['drain_timeout']}s") print(f" Requests completed: {active_connections['connections_completed']}") # Reboot impact analysis reboot_impact = { 'jobs_not_processed': active_connections['active_requests'] - Example 3: Reboot Multiple Instances in Sequence for Patching

Apply OS patches to multiple instances by rebooting them sequentially to maintain service availability (rolling update).

#!/bin/bash
# Sequential reboot for OS patching
INSTANCES=("i-0abc1def2ghi3jk4" "i-0xyz9abc8def7ghi" "i-0lmn5opq6rst7uvw")
TARGET_GROUP="arn:aws:elasticloadbalancing:us-east-1:123456789012:targetgroup/django-app/abc123"

echo "Rolling update: Patch and reboot instances sequentially"
echo "Total instances: ${#INSTANCES[@]}"
echo ""

for ((i=0; i<${#INSTANCES[@]}; i++)); do
  INSTANCE_ID=${INSTANCES[$i]}
  INSTANCE_NUM=$((i + 1))
  
  echo "========================================="
  echo "Instance $INSTANCE_NUM/${#INSTANCES[@]}: $INSTANCE_ID"
  echo "========================================="
  
  # Deregister from load balancer
  echo "Deregistering from ALB..."
  aws elbv2 deregister-targets \
    --target-group-arn $TARGET_GROUP \
    --targets Id=$INSTANCE_ID \
    --region us-east-1
  
  sleep 10  # Connection draining
  
  # Reboot
  echo "Rebooting instance..."
  aws ec2 reboot-instances \
    --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
    --region us-east-1
  
  # Wait for healthy status
  echo "Waiting for instance to be healthy..."
  aws ec2 wait instance-status-ok \
    --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
    --region us-east-1
  
  # Re-register with load balancer
  echo "Re-registering with ALB..."
  aws elbv2 register-targets \
    --target-group-arn $TARGET_GROUP \
    --targets Id=$INSTANCE_ID \
    --region us-east-1
  
  sleep 10  # Wait for ALB to mark healthy
  
  echo "✓ Instance $INSTANCE_NUM ready"
  echo ""
done

echo "========================================="
echo "✓ All instances patched and rebooted"
echo "✓ Service maintained throughout update"
echo "========================================="
Rolling update: Patch and reboot instances sequentially Total instances: 3 ========================================= Instance 1/3: i-0abc1def2ghi3jk4 ========================================= Deregistering from ALB... {} Rebooting instance... {} Waiting for instance to be healthy... (auto-waiter polls status) ✓ Instance 1 ready ========================================= Instance 2/3: i-0xyz9abc8def7ghi ========================================= Deregistering from ALB... {} Rebooting instance... {} Waiting for instance to be healthy... ✓ Instance 2 ready ========================================= Instance 3/3: i-0lmn5opq6rst7uvw ========================================= Deregistering from ALB... {} Rebooting instance... {} Waiting for instance to be healthy... ✓ Instance 3 ready ========================================= ✓ All instances patched and rebooted ✓ Service maintained throughout update =========================================
# Rolling update with sequential reboots for patching from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost from django.utils import timezone import time # Rolling update context rolling_update = { 'total_instances': 3, 'instances': [ 'i-0abc1def2ghi3jk4', 'i-0xyz9abc8def7ghi', 'i-0lmn5opq6rst7uvw' ], 'patch_type': 'OS security updates', 'strategy': 'Rolling update - one at a time' } print(f"Rolling Update - OS Patching") print(f"Strategy: {rolling_update['strategy']}") print(f"Instances to patch: {rolling_update['total_instances']}") # Track reboot progress reboot_log = [] for idx, instance_id in enumerate(rolling_update['instances'], 1): log_entry = { 'instance_number': idx, 'instance_id': instance_id, 'status': 'deregistered_from_alb', 'reboot_initiated': True, 'recovery_status': 'healthy', 'reregistered_alb': True, 'timestamp': timezone.now().isoformat() } reboot_log.append(log_entry) print(f"\nInstance {idx}/3: {instance_id}") print(f" Deregistered from ALB: ✓") print(f" Reboot initiated: ✓") print(f" Recovery status: {log_entry['recovery_status']}") print(f" Re-registered with ALB: ✓") # Application availability during update availability = { 'instances_healthy': rolling_update['total_instances'], 'jobs_accessible': JobPost.objects.count(), 'users_served': User.objects.filter(is_active=True).count(), 'service_continuity': 'Maintained (ALB routed to healthy instances)' } print(f"\nApplication availability during update:") print(f" Healthy instances serving traffic: {availability['instances_healthy']}") print(f" Jobs accessible: {availability['jobs_accessible']}") print(f" Active users served: {availability['users_served']}") print(f" Service continuity: {availability['service_continuity']}") # Update summary summary = { 'total_reboot_time_minutes': 15, 'downtime_per_user': 0, 'patches_applied': 12, 'security_updated': True, 'all_healthy': True } print(f"\nUpdate summary:") print(f" Total update time: {summary['total_reboot_time_minutes']} minutes") print(f" User-facing downtime: {summary['downtime_per_user']} minutes") print(f" Security patches applied: {summary['patches_applied']}") print(f"\n✓ All instances patched and healthy") print(f"✓ Zero-downtime achieved")
Example 4: Reboot with Health Check and Automatic Rollback

Reboot instance with immediate health verification, and automatic recovery if instance fails to reach healthy status.

#!/bin/bash
# Reboot with health check and rollback capability
INSTANCE_ID="i-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
SNAPSHOT_ID="snap-preboot123456"  # Pre-reboot snapshot
RECOVERY_TIMEOUT=300  # 5 minutes

echo "Reboot with automatic health verification"
echo "Instance: $INSTANCE_ID"
echo "Recovery timeout: ${RECOVERY_TIMEOUT}s"

# Create pre-reboot snapshot for rollback
echo ""
echo "Creating pre-reboot snapshot for rollback capability..."
VOLUME_ID=$(aws ec2 describe-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --query 'Reservations[0].Instances[0].BlockDeviceMappings[0].Ebs.VolumeId' \
  --output text \
  --region us-east-1)

PRE_BOOT_SNAP=$(aws ec2 create-snapshot \
  --volume-id $VOLUME_ID \
  --description "Pre-reboot snapshot for $INSTANCE_ID" \
  --region us-east-1 \
  --query 'SnapshotId' \
  --output text)

echo "✓ Pre-reboot snapshot: $PRE_BOOT_SNAP"

# Reboot the instance
echo ""
echo "Initiating reboot..."
aws ec2 reboot-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Reboot initiated"

# Monitor for successful health check
echo ""
echo "Monitoring instance health status (timeout: ${RECOVERY_TIMEOUT}s)..."

ELAPSED=0
INTERVAL=10

while [ $ELAPSED -lt $RECOVERY_TIMEOUT ]; do
  INSTANCE_STATUS=$(aws ec2 describe-instance-status \
    --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
    --query 'InstanceStatuses[0].InstanceStatus.Status' \
    --output text \
    --region us-east-1 2>/dev/null)
  
  if [ "$INSTANCE_STATUS" == "ok" ]; then
    echo ""
    echo "✓ Instance health check PASSED"
    exit 0
  fi
  
  echo "  Status: $INSTANCE_STATUS (${ELAPSED}s elapsed)"
  sleep $INTERVAL
  ELAPSED=$((ELAPSED + INTERVAL))
done

# If we reach here, reboot failed
echo ""
echo "✗ Instance health check FAILED after ${RECOVERY_TIMEOUT}s"
echo "Attempting automatic recovery..."
echo "  - Snapshot available: $PRE_BOOT_SNAP"
echo "  - Manual recovery required"
Reboot with automatic health verification Instance: i-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8 Recovery timeout: 300s Creating pre-reboot snapshot for rollback capability... ✓ Pre-reboot snapshot: snap-preboot123456 Initiating reboot... ✓ Reboot initiated Monitoring instance health status (timeout: 300s)... Status: initializing (10s elapsed) Status: initializing (20s elapsed) Status: initializing (30s elapsed) Status: ok (45s elapsed) ✓ Instance health check PASSED
# Instance reboot with health verification from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost from django.utils import timezone from django.db import connection import time health_check = { 'instance_id': 'i-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8', 'reboot_type': 'with health verification', 'recovery_timeout_seconds': 300, 'pre_reboot_snapshot': 'snap-preboot123456' } print(f"Instance Reboot - Health Verification") print(f"Instance: {health_check['instance_id']}") print(f"Recovery timeout: {health_check['recovery_timeout_seconds']}s") # Database connectivity check before reboot pre_reboot_db = { 'connection_status': 'connected', 'queries_executed': 4, 'response_time_ms': 12 } print(f"\nPre-reboot database status:") print(f" Connection: {pre_reboot_db['connection_status']}") print(f" Recent queries: {pre_reboot_db['queries_executed']}") # Application health check pre_reboot_app = { 'skills': Skills.objects.count(), 'authors': Author.objects.count(), 'jobs': JobPost.objects.count(), 'locations': Location.objects.count(), 'total_records': Skills.objects.count() + Author.objects.count() + JobPost.objects.count() + Location.objects.count() } print(f"\nPre-reboot application state:") print(f" Total records: {pre_reboot_app['total_records']}") # Health check sequence during reboot health_sequence = [ {'elapsed_seconds': 10, 'status': 'initializing', 'description': 'System starting'}, {'elapsed_seconds': 20, 'status': 'initializing', 'description': 'Services loading'}, {'elapsed_seconds': 30, 'status': 'initializing', 'description': 'Database connection'}, {'elapsed_seconds': 45, 'status': 'ok', 'description': 'Fully healthy'} ] print(f"\nHealth check progression:") for check in health_sequence: print(f" {check['elapsed_seconds']:3d}s: {check['status']:15s} - {check['description']}") # Post-reboot validation post_reboot = { 'timestamp': timezone.now().isoformat(), 'system_healthy': True, 'database_accessible': True, 'app_state_intact': pre_reboot_app['total_records'] > 0, 'recovery_time_seconds': 45 } print(f"\nPost-reboot validation:") print(f" System healthy: {post_reboot['system_healthy']}") print(f" Database accessible: {post_reboot['database_accessible']}") print(f" Recovery time: {post_reboot['recovery_time_seconds']}s") print(f"\n✓ Reboot completed successfully") print(f"✓ All health checks passed") print(f"✓ No manual intervention needed")
Example 5: Reboot with Performance Baseline Comparison

Reboot instance and compare performance metrics before and after to verify system efficiency improvements (e.g., memory leaks cleared, kernel optimizations).

#!/bin/bash
# Reboot with performance comparison
INSTANCE_ID="i-0lmn5opq6rst7uvw"
NAMESPACE="AWS/EC2"

echo "Instance reboot with performance baseline comparison"
echo "Instance: $INSTANCE_ID"

# Capture pre-reboot metrics (last hour)
echo ""
echo "Collecting pre-reboot metrics..."

PRE_REBOOT_CPU=$(aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
  --namespace $NAMESPACE \
  --metric-name CPUUtilization \
  --dimensions Name=InstanceId,Value=$INSTANCE_ID \
  --start-time $(date -u -d '1 hour ago' +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S) \
  --end-time $(date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S) \
  --period 300 \
  --statistics Average \
  --query 'Datapoints[*].Average' \
  --output text \
  --region us-east-1)

echo "✓ Pre-reboot metrics captured"

# Perform reboot
echo ""
echo "Initiating reboot..."
aws ec2 reboot-instances \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

# Wait for recovery
aws ec2 wait instance-status-ok \
  --instance-ids $INSTANCE_ID \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Reboot completed"

# Allow time for post-reboot stabilization
echo "Waiting for post-reboot stabilization (2 minutes)..."
sleep 120

# Capture post-reboot metrics
echo ""
echo "Collecting post-reboot metrics..."

POST_REBOOT_CPU=$(aws cloudwatch get-metric-statistics \
  --namespace $NAMESPACE \
  --metric-name CPUUtilization \
  --dimensions Name=InstanceId,Value=$INSTANCE_ID \
  --start-time $(date -u -d '2 minutes ago' +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S) \
  --end-time $(date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S) \
  --period 300 \
  --statistics Average \
  --query 'Datapoints[*].Average' \
  --output text \
  --region us-east-1)

echo "✓ Post-reboot metrics captured"

echo ""
echo "Performance comparison:"
echo "  Pre-reboot average CPU: $(echo $PRE_REBOOT_CPU | awk '{print $NF}')%"
echo "  Post-reboot average CPU: $(echo $POST_REBOOT_CPU | awk '{print $NF}')%"
echo ""
echo "Metric analysis complete"

Collecting post-reboot metrics... ✓ Post-reboot metrics captured Performance comparison: Pre-reboot average CPU: 72% Post-reboot average CPU: 48% Metric analysis complete

create-security-group

Creates a security group that acts as a firewall controlling inbound and outbound traffic to EC2 instances. Security groups define which protocols, ports, and IP addresses are allowed to communicate with your instances. Essential for Django application access control and network isolation.

Syntax
aws ec2 create-security-group \
  --group-name {name} \
  --description '{description}' \
  --vpc-id {vpc-id} \
  --region {region}
Parameters Description
  • --group-name (string, required): Name of the security group. Cannot contain spaces or special characters
  • --description (string, required): Description of what this security group is for
  • --vpc-id (string): VPC ID where security group is created. If omitted, uses default VPC
  • --region (string): AWS region where security group will be created
Return Value
  • GroupId (string): ID of the newly created security group (sg-xxxxxxxxx)
  • GroupName (string): Name of the security group
  • VpcId (string): VPC where security group was created
  • Tags (Array): Any tags attached to the security group
5 Detailed EC2 create-security-group Examples
Example 1: Create Django Application Security Group for Web Traffic

Create a security group for Django web application allowing HTTP/HTTPS traffic from the internet.

#!/bin/bash
# Create Django web application security group
VPC_ID="vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "Creating Django Web Application Security Group..."

# Create the security group
SG_RESPONSE=$(aws ec2 create-security-group \
  --group-name django-web-app \
  --description "Security group for Django web application - allows HTTP/HTTPS from internet" \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --region $REGION)

SG_ID=$(echo $SG_RESPONSE | jq -r '.GroupId')

echo "✓ Security Group Created: $SG_ID"
echo "  Name: django-web-app"
echo "  VPC: $VPC_ID"

# Add tags for identification
aws ec2 create-tags \
  --resources $SG_ID \
  --tags Key=Name,Value=django-web-app Key=Environment,Value=production Key=Application,Value=jobpost \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Tags applied"
echo ""
echo "Security Group Details:"
echo "  Group ID: $SG_ID"
echo "  Group Name: django-web-app"
echo "  Description: Security group for Django web application - allows HTTP/HTTPS from internet"
echo ""
echo "Next steps:"
echo "  1. Add inbound rules (authorize-security-group-ingress)"
echo "  2. Attach to EC2 instances"
echo "  3. Configure database and cache security groups"

Add inbound rules (authorize-security-group-ingress) 2. Attach to EC2 instances 3. Configure database and cache security groups

Example 2: Create Database Security Group for MySQL Access

Create a dedicated security group for RDS MySQL database that only allows traffic from web application security group.

#!/bin/bash
# Create RDS database security group
VPC_ID="vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
REGION="us-east-1"

# Create the security group
SG_RESPONSE=$(aws ec2 create-security-group \
  --group-name django-database \
  --description "Security group for RDS MySQL - allows access only from Django app security group" \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --region $REGION)

DB_SG_ID=$(echo $SG_RESPONSE | jq -r '.GroupId')

echo "✓ Database Security Group Created: $DB_SG_ID"

# Add tags
aws ec2 create-tags \
  --resources $DB_SG_ID \
  --tags Key=Name,Value=django-database Key=Environment,Value=production Key=Database,Value=mysql-rds \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Tags applied to database security group"
echo ""
echo "Database Security Group Details:"
echo "  Group ID: $DB_SG_ID"
echo "  Purpose: RDS MySQL database access"
echo ""
echo "Important:"
echo "  - This security group is empty (no inbound rules yet)"
echo "  - You must authorize inbound traffic from django-web-app security group"
echo "  - MySQL port 3306 will be accessible only from web app instances"

{model_name}") print(f"\n✓ Database security group created") print(f"✓ Ready for inbound rules configuration")

authorize-security-group-ingress

Adds inbound traffic rules to a security group, allowing specific protocols, ports, and source IPs/security groups to communicate with instances. This is how you open up access to Django applications (HTTP/HTTPS), databases (MySQL/PostgreSQL), and cache systems (Redis).

Syntax
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id {sg-id} \
  --protocol {tcp|udp|icmp|-1} \
  --port {port-number} \
  --cidr {cidr-block} \
  --region {region}
Parameters Description
  • --group-id (string, required): Security group ID to add rule to (sg-xxxxxxxxx)
  • --protocol (string, required): Protocol type - tcp, udp, icmp, or -1 for all
  • --port (string): Port number or port range (e.g., 80 or 8000-8100)
  • --cidr (string): CIDR block allowing access (e.g., 0.0.0.0/0 for internet, 10.0.0.0/16 for VPC)
  • --source-security-group-id (string): Allow traffic from another security group instead of CIDR
  • --description (string): Description of what this rule is for
Return Value
  • Return (boolean): True if rule was successfully added
  • SecurityGroupRules (Array): Details of the rule that was added
5 Detailed EC2 authorize-security-group-ingress Examples
Example 1: Allow HTTP and HTTPS from Internet to ALB

Add inbound rules to ALB security group allowing internet traffic on standard web ports.

#!/bin/bash
# Add HTTP/HTTPS inbound rules to ALB security group
ALB_SG="sg-3c4d5e6f7g8h9i0j1"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "Adding HTTP and HTTPS rules to ALB security group..."

# Add HTTP rule (port 80)
echo "Adding HTTP (port 80) rule..."
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $ALB_SG \
  --protocol tcp \
  --port 80 \
  --cidr 0.0.0.0/0 \
  --description "HTTP from internet" \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ HTTP rule added"

# Add HTTPS rule (port 443)
echo "Adding HTTPS (port 443) rule..."
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $ALB_SG \
  --protocol tcp \
  --port 443 \
  --cidr 0.0.0.0/0 \
  --description "HTTPS from internet" \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ HTTPS rule added"
echo ""

echo "  ✓ HTTPS (port 443) from 0.0.0.0/0"
echo ""

authorize-security-group-egress

Adds outbound traffic rules to a security group, controlling what traffic instances can send out. By default, all outbound traffic is allowed, but you can restrict it to specific destinations (databases, APIs, cache systems) for enhanced security. Essential for Django apps communicating with RDS, Redis, external APIs, and package repositories.

Syntax
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-egress \
  --group-id {sg-id} \
  --protocol {tcp|udp|icmp|-1} \
  --port {port-number} \
  --cidr {cidr-block} \
  --region {region}
Parameters Description
  • --group-id (string, required): Security group ID to add rule to (sg-xxxxxxxxx)
  • --protocol (string, required): Protocol type - tcp, udp, icmp, or -1 for all
  • --port (string): Port number or port range (e.g., 443 for HTTPS, 3306 for MySQL)
  • --cidr (string): CIDR block for destination (e.g., 0.0.0.0/0 for all, 10.0.0.0/16 for VPC)
  • --destination-security-group-id (string): Allow traffic to another security group
  • --description (string): Description of what this rule allows
Return Value
  • Return (boolean): True if rule was successfully added
  • SecurityGroupRules (Array): Details of the rule that was added
5 Detailed EC2 authorize-security-group-egress Examples
Example 1: Allow Django Instances to Access External APIs (HTTPS Only)

Restrict outbound traffic to HTTPS on port 443 for calling third-party APIs (payment, email, authentication services).

#!/bin/bash
# Allow Django instances to call external APIs via HTTPS
APP_SG="sg-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "Configuring outbound HTTPS access for external APIs..."

# First, remove the default allow-all outbound rule
echo "Removing default allow-all outbound rule..."
aws ec2 revoke-security-group-egress \
  --group-id $APP_SG \
  --ip-permissions IpProtocol=-1,IpRanges='[{CidrIp=0.0.0.0/0}]' \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Default rule removed"

# Add specific HTTPS rule for external APIs
echo "Adding HTTPS (port 443) outbound rule..."
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-egress \
  --group-id $APP_SG \
  --protocol tcp \
  --port 443 \
  --cidr 0.0.0.0/0 \
  --description "HTTPS to external APIs (payment, email, auth services)" \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ HTTPS outbound rule added"

# Also allow DNS (port 53) for domain lookups
echo "Adding DNS (port 53) outbound rule..."
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-egress \
  --group-id $APP_SG \
  --protocol udp \
  --port 53 \
  --cidr 0.0.0.0/0 \
  --description "DNS for domain name resolution" \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ DNS rule added"
echo ""
echo "Outbound access configured:"
echo "  ✓ HTTPS (443) to external APIs"
echo "  ✓ DNS (53) for domain resolution"
echo "  ✗ HTTP (80) blocked for security"
echo "  ✗ SSH (22) blocked"
echo ""
echo "Django instances can now:"
echo "  - Call payment APIs (Stripe, PayPal)"
echo "  - Send emails via SES/SendGrid"
echo "  - Authenticate with OAuth providers"
echo "  - Download packages from PyPI (port 443)"

Example 3: Allow Django to Access Redis Cache (Outbound)

Configure outbound access from Django instances to Redis cache for session storage and query caching.

#!/bin/bash
# Allow Django instances outbound access to Redis cache
APP_SG="sg-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
CACHE_SG="sg-2b3c4d5e6f7g8h9i0"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "Configuring Django outbound access to Redis cache..."

# Add Redis outbound rule
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-egress \
  --group-id $APP_SG \
  --protocol tcp \
  --port 6379 \
  --destination-security-group-id $CACHE_SG \
  --description "Redis cache access (outbound)" \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Redis outbound rule added"
echo ""
echo "Cache access configured:"
echo "  Source: django-web-app ($APP_SG)"
echo "  Destination: django-cache ($CACHE_SG)"

echo "  - Implement rate limiting"

Example 5: Restrict Outbound to Internal VPC Only (Zero-Trust Network)

Implement zero-trust networking by removing default all-allow rule and only allowing traffic to internal VPC resources.

#!/bin/bash
# Implement zero-trust: restrict outbound to VPC only
APP_SG="sg-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
VPC_CIDR="10.0.0.0/16"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "Implementing zero-trust network security..."
echo "Removing default allow-all outbound rule..."

# Remove default allow-all rule
aws ec2 revoke-security-group-egress \
  --group-id $APP_SG \
  --ip-permissions IpProtocol=-1,IpRanges='[{CidrIp=0.0.0.0/0}]' \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Default rule removed"

# Add specific outbound rules for internal services only

# Allow traffic to database
echo "Adding outbound to database security group..."
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-egress \
  --group-id $APP_SG \
  --protocol tcp \
  --port 3306 \
  --cidr 10.0.2.0/24 \
  --description "MySQL database (private subnet)" \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Database rule added"

# Allow traffic to cache
echo "Adding outbound to cache security group..."
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-egress \
  --group-id $APP_SG \
  --protocol tcp \
  --port 6379 \
  --cidr 10.0.3.0/24 \
  --description "Redis cache (private subnet)" \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Cache rule added"

# Allow DNS within VPC
echo "Adding outbound DNS within VPC..."
aws ec2 authorize-security-group-egress \
  --group-id $APP_SG \
  --protocol udp \
  --port 53 \
  --cidr $VPC_CIDR \
  --description "DNS within VPC" \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ DNS rule added"

echo ""
echo "Zero-trust security configured:"
echo "  ✗ No internet access"
echo "  ✓ Only internal VPC traffic allowed"
echo "  ✓ Database access: 10.0.2.0/24"
echo "  ✓ Cache access: 10.0.3.0/24"
echo "  ✓ DNS within VPC: 10.0.0.0/16"
