{ "Return": true, "SecurityGroupRules": [{ "GroupId": "sg-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8", "GroupOwnerId": "123456789012", "SecurityGroupRuleId": "sgr-egress-mysql", "IpProtocol": "tcp", "FromPort": 3306, "ToPort": 3306, "ReferencedGroupInfo": { "GroupId": "sg-1a2b3c4d5e6f7g8h9", "GroupOwnerId": "123456789012" }, "IsEgress": true }] } ✓ MySQL outbound rule added Database access configured: Source: django-web-app (sg-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8) Destination: django-database (sg-1a2b3c4d5e6f7g8h9)

describe-security-groups

Retrieve information about security groups, including details about their rules, tags, and associated resources. Useful for querying security group configuration and verifying network access rules.

Syntax
aws ec2 describe-security-groups \
  [--group-ids ] \
  [--group-names ] \
  [--filters Name=,Values=] \
  [--region ]
Parameters Description
  • --group-ids (list): One or more security group IDs to describe. When specified, only these groups are returned. Multiple IDs can be provided as space-separated values.
  • --group-names (list): One or more security group names to describe. This only works for security groups in the default VPC. For VPC security groups, use --group-ids instead.
  • --filters (list): Filter results by specific attributes. Common filters include group-name, vpc-id, tag-key, tag-value, group-id. Format: Name=key,Values=value1 value2
  • --region (string): AWS region where the security groups are located (us-east-1, eu-west-1, etc.)
  • --max-results (integer): Maximum number of results to return per page (default 1000)
  • --next-token (string): Token for pagination to retrieve next batch of results
Return Value
  • SecurityGroups (Array): List of security group objects with detailed configuration
  • GroupId (String): Unique security group identifier (sg-xxxxxxxx)
  • GroupName (String): Human-readable name of the security group
  • VpcId (String): VPC containing the security group
  • IpPermissions (Array): Inbound rules for the security group
  • IpPermissionsEgress (Array): Outbound rules for the security group
  • Tags (Array): Key-value tags associated with the security group
  • OwnerId (String): AWS account ID that owns the security group
Example 1: List All Security Groups in VPC

Retrieve all security groups in a specific VPC and display their details for auditing and verification.

#!/bin/bash
# List all security groups in a VPC
VPC_ID="vpc-12345678"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "Listing all security groups in VPC: $VPC_ID"
echo ""

aws ec2 describe-security-groups \
  --filters Name=vpc-id,Values=$VPC_ID \
  --region $REGION \
  --query 'SecurityGroups[*].[GroupId,GroupName,VpcId]' \
  --output table

echo ""
echo "Query results:"
echo "  - GroupId: Unique security group identifier"
echo "  - GroupName: Human-readable name"
echo "  - VpcId: VPC containing the security group"

revoke-security-group-ingress

Remove inbound rules from a security group. Used to revoke network access that was previously granted. Useful for restricting access, removing outdated rules, or cleaning up security group configurations.

Syntax
aws ec2 revoke-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id  \
  --protocol  \
  --port  \
  --cidr  | --source-security-group-id  \
  [--region ]
Parameters Description
  • --group-id (string): The ID of the security group to revoke rules from. Format: sg-xxxxxxxx
  • --protocol (string): The protocol number or name (tcp, udp, icmp, or -1 for all). Use 'tcp' for HTTP/HTTPS/MySQL, 'udp' for DNS.
  • --port (integer): The port or port range to revoke (e.g., 80, 443, 3306, 6379). Omit for protocols that don't use ports.
  • --cidr (string): The CIDR block to revoke access from (e.g., 0.0.0.0/0 for public, 10.0.0.0/8 for private VPC).
  • --source-security-group-id (string): Another security group ID instead of CIDR. Allows traffic from instances in that group.
  • --region (string): AWS region where the security group is located (us-east-1, eu-west-1, etc.)
Return Value
  • Return (boolean): True if the rule was successfully revoked, false otherwise
  • UnknownIpPermissions (Array): Rules that couldn't be found to revoke (may indicate rule already removed)
  • SecurityGroupRuleId (String): ID of the revoked rule for tracking purposes
Example 1: Revoke Public SSH Access from Security Group

Remove SSH port 22 access from all public internet (0.0.0.0/0) to tighten security and restrict administrative access.

#!/bin/bash
# Revoke public SSH access for security hardening
APP_SG="sg-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "Revoking public SSH access from security group..."
echo "Before: SSH (port 22) open to 0.0.0.0/0"
echo ""

# Remove the public SSH rule
aws ec2 revoke-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $APP_SG \
  --protocol tcp \
  --port 22 \
  --cidr 0.0.0.0/0 \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ SSH rule revoked"
echo ""
echo "After revocation:"
echo "  SSH access: DENIED from public internet"
echo "  SSH access: ALLOWED from VPN only (if configured)"
echo "  Security posture: IMPROVED"
Revoking public SSH access from security group... Before: SSH (port 22) open to 0.0.0.0/0 { "Return": true, "SecurityGroupRules": [{ "GroupId": "sg-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8", "SecurityGroupRuleId": "sgr-revoked-ssh", "IpProtocol": "tcp", "FromPort": 22, "ToPort": 22, "CidrIpv4": "0.0.0.0/0", "IsEgress": false }] } ✓ SSH rule revoked After revocation: SSH access: DENIED from public internet SSH access: ALLOWED from VPN only Security posture: IMPROVED

Example 3: Revoke Database Access from Old Application Tier

Example 5: Revoke Access After Security Incident

Quickly revoke access from a security group as part of incident response when suspicious activity is detected.

#!/bin/bash
# Incident response: Revoke access after suspicious activity
AFFECTED_SG="sg-2b3c4d5e6f7g8h9i0"
ATTACKER_CIDR="198.51.100.0/24"  # Suspicious source
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "⚠ SECURITY INCIDENT RESPONSE"
echo "Revoking access from suspicious source..."
echo "Source: $ATTACKER_CIDR"
echo ""

# Revoke all TCP traffic from suspicious source
aws ec2 revoke-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $AFFECTED_SG \
  --protocol tcp \
  --port 0-65535 \
  --cidr $ATTACKER_CIDR \
  --region $REGION

# Alternative: revoke all protocols
aws ec2 revoke-security-group-ingress \
  --group-id $AFFECTED_SG \
  --protocol -1 \
  --cidr $ATTACKER_CIDR \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Suspicious traffic blocked"
echo ""
echo "Incident response actions:"
echo "  1. ✓ Access revoked"
echo "  2. → Enable WAF rules"
echo "  3. → Review CloudTrail logs"
echo "  4. → Notify security team"
echo "  5. → Document incident"

revoke-security-group-egress

Remove outbound rules from a security group. Used to revoke network access that was previously granted for outbound traffic. Useful for implementing zero-trust networking and restricting external communication.

Syntax
aws ec2 revoke-security-group-egress \
  --group-id  \
  --protocol  \
  --port  \
  --cidr  | --destination-security-group-id  \
  [--region ]
Parameters Description
  • --group-id (string): The ID of the security group to revoke egress rules from. Format: sg-xxxxxxxx
  • --protocol (string): The protocol number or name (tcp, udp, icmp, or -1 for all). Use 'tcp' for HTTP/HTTPS/MySQL, 'udp' for DNS.
  • --port (integer): The port or port range to revoke (e.g., 80, 443, 3306, 6379). Omit for protocols that don't use ports.
  • --cidr (string): The CIDR block to revoke outbound access to (e.g., 0.0.0.0/0 for internet, 10.0.0.0/8 for VPC).
  • --destination-security-group-id (string): Another security group ID instead of CIDR. Revokes traffic to that group.
  • --region (string): AWS region where the security group is located (us-east-1, eu-west-1, etc.)
Return Value
  • Return (boolean): True if the rule was successfully revoked, false otherwise
  • UnknownIpPermissions (Array): Rules that couldn't be found to revoke (may indicate rule already removed)
  • SecurityGroupRuleId (String): ID of the revoked rule for tracking purposes
Example 1: Revoke Public Internet Access for Zero-Trust Network

Remove all outbound access to 0.0.0.0/0 to implement zero-trust networking where only specific internal resources are accessible.

#!/bin/bash
# Implement zero-trust: revoke default allow-all outbound rule
APP_SG="sg-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "Implementing zero-trust network security..."
echo "Revoking default allow-all outbound rule..."
echo ""

# Remove default allow-all egress rule
aws ec2 revoke-security-group-egress \
  --group-id $APP_SG \
  --protocol -1 \
  --cidr 0.0.0.0/0 \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Default allow-all rule revoked"
echo ""
echo "Outbound restrictions activated:"
echo "  Public internet: DENIED"
echo "  Database (10.0.2.0/24): Available via specific rules"
echo "  Cache (10.0.3.0/24): Available via specific rules"
echo "  DNS (port 53): Available via specific rules"
echo ""
echo "Next: Add specific authorize-security-group-egress rules"

Example 5: Revoke All Egress Rules for Forensic Isolation

Remove all outbound rules during forensic investigation to prevent any communication while analyzing a potentially compromised instance.

#!/bin/bash
# Forensic isolation: Revoke all outbound access
COMPROMISED_SG="sg-5e6f7g8h9i0j1k2l3"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "🔒 FORENSIC ISOLATION IN PROGRESS"
echo "Revoking all outbound access..."
echo ""

# Revoke all protocols (tcp, udp, icmp, all)
aws ec2 revoke-security-group-egress \
  --group-id $COMPROMISED_SG \
  --protocol -1 \
  --cidr 0.0.0.0/0 \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ All outbound rules revoked"
echo ""
echo "Instance isolation status:"
echo "  Internet access: BLOCKED"
echo "  Internal VPC access: BLOCKED"
echo "  All outbound: BLOCKED"
echo ""
echo "Forensic investigation:"
echo "  Instance state: ISOLATED"
echo "  SSH access: Via Systems Manager Session Manager"
echo "  Data collection: Via EBS snapshot"
echo "  Next steps: Forensic analysis of logs/memory"

create-vpc

Create a Virtual Private Cloud (VPC) - an isolated network environment for your AWS infrastructure. A VPC is the foundation for deploying applications with complete control over IP addressing, subnets, routing, and security.

Syntax
aws ec2 create-vpc \
  --cidr-block  \
  [--tag-specifications 'ResourceType=vpc,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=}]'] \
  [--region ]
Parameters Description
  • --cidr-block (string): The IPv4 address range for the VPC in CIDR notation (e.g., 10.0.0.0/16). This is the primary IP address block for the VPC. Choose /16 for large deployments or /20 for smaller ones.
  • --tag-specifications (string): Tags to apply to the VPC for organization and billing. Format: ResourceType=vpc,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=my-vpc}]
  • --amazon-provided-ipv6-cidr-block (boolean): Request an IPv6 CIDR block for the VPC (optional, for IPv6 support)
  • --region (string): AWS region where the VPC is created (us-east-1, eu-west-1, etc.)
  • --enable-dns-hostnames (boolean): Enable DNS hostnames in the VPC (useful for application domain names)
  • --enable-dns-support (boolean): Enable DNS support to allow instances to resolve domain names
Return Value
  • Vpc (Object): The created VPC object with detailed information
  • VpcId (String): Unique VPC identifier (vpc-xxxxxxxx)
  • CidrBlock (String): The IPv4 CIDR block assigned to the VPC
  • State (String): Current VPC state (pending, available)
  • IsDefault (Boolean): True if this is the default VPC, false for custom VPCs
  • Tags (Array): Tags applied to the VPC for identification
  • OwnerId (String): AWS account ID that owns the VPC
Example 1: Create Production VPC with /16 CIDR Block

Create a production VPC with a large IP address space (/16) to accommodate multiple subnets across availability zones.

#!/bin/bash
# Create production VPC for Django application
CIDR_BLOCK="10.0.0.0/16"
REGION="us-east-1"
VPC_NAME="anihpj-production-vpc"

echo "Creating production VPC..."
echo "CIDR Block: $CIDR_BLOCK"
echo ""

# Create VPC with tags
VPC_ID=$(aws ec2 create-vpc \
  --cidr-block $CIDR_BLOCK \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=vpc,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=$VPC_NAME},{Key=Environment,Value=production}]" \
  --region $REGION \
  --query 'Vpc.VpcId' \
  --output text)

echo "✓ VPC created"
echo "VPC ID: $VPC_ID"
echo ""

# Enable DNS support
aws ec2 modify-vpc-attribute \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --enable-dns-hostnames \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ DNS hostnames enabled"
echo ""
echo "VPC Configuration:"
echo "  VPC ID: $VPC_ID"
echo "  CIDR Block: $CIDR_BLOCK"
echo "  Available subnets: 256 (with /24 subnets)"
echo "  IP address space: 65,536 IPs"

  --output table

Example 4: Create VPC for Multi-Region Deployment

Create VPCs in multiple regions for disaster recovery and geographic distribution of the Django application.

#!/bin/bash
# Create VPCs in multiple regions for DR and geo-distribution
declare -A regions=(
  ["us-east-1"]="10.0.0.0/16"
  ["eu-west-1"]="10.1.0.0/16"
  ["ap-southeast-1"]="10.2.0.0/16"
)

echo "Creating VPCs for multi-region deployment..."
echo ""

for region in "${!regions[@]}"; do
  cidr=${regions[$region]}
  vpc_name="anihpj-vpc-$region"
  
  echo "Creating VPC in $region: $cidr"
  
  vpc_id=$(aws ec2 create-vpc \
    --cidr-block $cidr \
    --tag-specifications "ResourceType=vpc,Tags=[
      {Key=Name,Value=$vpc_name},
      {Key=Environment,Value=production},
      {Key=Region,Value=$region},
      {Key=DisasterRecovery,Value=enabled}
    ]" \
    --region $region \
    --query 'Vpc.VpcId' \
    --output text)
  
  echo "  VPC ID: $vpc_id"
  
  # Enable DNS
  aws ec2 modify-vpc-attribute \
    --vpc-id $vpc_id \
    --enable-dns-hostnames \
    --region $region
  
  echo "  ✓ DNS enabled"
  echo ""
done

echo "Multi-region VPC deployment complete"
echo "VPCs ready for peering and replication"
Creating VPCs for multi-region deployment... Creating VPC in us-east-1: 10.0.0.0/16 { "Vpc": { "VpcId": "vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8", "CidrBlock": "10.0.0.0/16", "State": "available" } } VPC ID: vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8 ✓ DNS enabled Creating VPC in eu-west-1: 10.1.0.0/16 { "Vpc": { "VpcId": "vpc-1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8i9", "CidrBlock": "10.1.0.0/16", "State": "available" } } VPC ID: vpc-1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8i9 ✓ DNS enabled Multi-region VPC deployment complete

Example 5: Create VPC with Secondary CIDR Block for Expansion

Create a VPC with multiple CIDR blocks to support future expansion without recreating the VPC.

#!/bin/bash
# Create VPC with primary CIDR, plan for secondary CIDR expansion
PRIMARY_CIDR="10.0.0.0/16"
SECONDARY_CIDR="10.1.0.0/16"
REGION="us-east-1"
VPC_NAME="anihpj-expandable-vpc"

echo "Creating VPC with expansion capability..."
echo "Primary CIDR: $PRIMARY_CIDR"
echo "Secondary CIDR (for future): $SECONDARY_CIDR"
echo ""

# Create VPC with primary CIDR
VPC_ID=$(aws ec2 create-vpc \
  --cidr-block $PRIMARY_CIDR \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=vpc,Tags=[
    {Key=Name,Value=$VPC_NAME},
    {Key=Environment,Value=production},
    {Key=ExpansionCapability,Value=enabled}
  ]" \
  --region $REGION \
  --query 'Vpc.VpcId' \
  --output text)

echo "✓ Primary VPC created"
echo "VPC ID: $VPC_ID"
echo ""

# Associate secondary CIDR (optional, for future expansion)
echo "Adding secondary CIDR for future expansion..."
aws ec2 associate-vpc-cidr-block \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block $SECONDARY_CIDR \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Secondary CIDR associated"
echo ""

# Enable DNS
aws ec2 modify-vpc-attribute \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --enable-dns-hostnames \
  --region $REGION

echo "VPC Configuration Summary:"
echo "  VPC ID: $VPC_ID"
echo "  Primary CIDR: $PRIMARY_CIDR (65,536 IPs)"
echo "  Secondary CIDR: $SECONDARY_CIDR (65,536 IPs)"
echo "  Total available: 131,072 IPs"
echo "  Expansion ready: YES"

create-subnet

Create a subnet within a VPC. Subnets divide your VPC into smaller network segments for organizing resources and controlling network traffic. Each subnet is associated with a single availability zone and can be public (internet-routable) or private (internal only).

Syntax
aws ec2 create-subnet \
  --vpc-id  \
  --cidr-block  \
  [--availability-zone ] \
  [--tag-specifications 'ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=}]'] \
  [--region ]
Parameters Description
  • --vpc-id (string): The ID of the VPC where the subnet will be created. Format: vpc-xxxxxxxx
  • --cidr-block (string): The IPv4 CIDR block for the subnet in CIDR notation (e.g., 10.0.1.0/24). Must be a subset of the VPC's CIDR block.
  • --availability-zone (string): The availability zone where the subnet will be created (us-east-1a, us-east-1b, etc.). Omit to let AWS choose.
  • --tag-specifications (string): Tags to apply to the subnet. Format: ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=my-subnet}]
  • --region (string): AWS region where the VPC is located (us-east-1, eu-west-1, etc.)
  • --ipv6-cidr-block (string): IPv6 CIDR block for the subnet (optional, for IPv6 support)
Return Value
  • Subnet (Object): The created subnet object with detailed information
  • SubnetId (String): Unique subnet identifier (subnet-xxxxxxxx)
  • VpcId (String): VPC containing the subnet
  • CidrBlock (String): The IPv4 CIDR block assigned to the subnet
  • AvailabilityZone (String): Availability zone where the subnet is located
  • State (String): Current subnet state (pending, available)
  • AvailableIpAddressCount (Integer): Number of available IP addresses in the subnet
  • Tags (Array): Tags applied to the subnet for identification
Example 1: Create Public Subnet for Web Tier

Create a public subnet in the first availability zone for hosting web servers and load balancers.

#!/bin/bash
# Create public subnet for web tier
VPC_ID="vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
SUBNET_CIDR="10.0.1.0/24"
AZ="us-east-1a"
REGION="us-east-1"
SUBNET_NAME="anihpj-public-web-1a"

echo "Creating public subnet for web tier..."
echo "VPC ID: $VPC_ID"
echo "CIDR: $SUBNET_CIDR"
echo "AZ: $AZ"
echo ""

# Create the public subnet
SUBNET_ID=$(aws ec2 create-subnet \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block $SUBNET_CIDR \
  --availability-zone $AZ \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[
    {Key=Name,Value=$SUBNET_NAME},
    {Key=Type,Value=Public},
    {Key=Layer,Value=Web}
  ]" \
  --region $REGION \
  --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' \
  --output text)

echo "✓ Subnet created"
echo "Subnet ID: $SUBNET_ID"
echo ""

# Enable auto-assign public IP
aws ec2 modify-subnet-attribute \
  --subnet-id $SUBNET_ID \
  --map-public-ip-on-launch \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Auto-assign public IP enabled"
echo ""
echo "Subnet details:"
echo "  Type: Public (routes to Internet Gateway)"
echo "  Layer: Web tier (ALB, web servers)"
echo "  Available IPs: 256 (minus 5 reserved)"

    {Key=Name,Value=$SUBNET_NAME},

Example 3: Create Database Subnet in Different AZ (Multi-AZ HA)

Create a database subnet in a different availability zone to enable multi-AZ RDS deployment for high availability.

#!/bin/bash
# Create private database subnet in second AZ
VPC_ID="vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
SUBNET_CIDR="10.0.20.0/24"
AZ="us-east-1b"
REGION="us-east-1"
SUBNET_NAME="anihpj-private-db-1b"

echo "Creating database subnet for multi-AZ HA..."
echo "VPC ID: $VPC_ID"
echo "CIDR: $SUBNET_CIDR"
echo "AZ: $AZ (different from app tier)"
echo ""

# Create the database subnet in AZ-1b
SUBNET_ID=$(aws ec2 create-subnet \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block $SUBNET_CIDR \
  --availability-zone $AZ \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[
    {Key=Name,Value=$SUBNET_NAME},
    {Key=Type,Value=Private},
    {Key=Layer,Value=Database},
    {Key=DBSubnetGroup,Value=anihpj-db-subnet-group}
  ]" \
  --region $REGION \
  --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' \
  --output text)

echo "✓ Subnet created"
echo "Subnet ID: $SUBNET_ID"
echo ""

echo "Multi-AZ RDS Configuration:"
echo "  Primary DB (AZ-1a): subnet-db-1a (10.0.20.0/24)"
echo "  Standby DB (AZ-1b): $SUBNET_ID (10.0.20.0/24) ← NEW"
echo "  Failover: Automatic (< 1 minute)"
echo "  Data replication: Synchronous"

RTO and RPO metrics disaster_recovery = { 'rto_recovery_time': '< 1 minute', 'rpo_data_loss': '0 transactions', 'availability': '99.95% SLA', 'backup_retention': '30 days' } print(f"\nDisaster Recovery metrics:") for metric, value in disaster_recovery.items(): print(f" {metric}: {value}") print(f"\n✓ Multi-AZ database subnet created") print(f"✓ High availability database ready")
Example 4: Create Multiple Subnets in Bulk Using Variables

Create multiple subnets at once for a complete multi-tier, multi-AZ infrastructure.

#!/bin/bash
# Create multiple subnets for complete infrastructure
VPC_ID="vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
REGION="us-east-1"

# Define subnets: NAME, CIDR, AZ
declare -A subnets=(
  ["public-web-1a"]="10.0.1.0/24:us-east-1a:Public"
  ["public-web-1b"]="10.0.2.0/24:us-east-1b:Public"
  ["private-app-1a"]="10.0.10.0/24:us-east-1a:Private"
  ["private-app-1b"]="10.0.11.0/24:us-east-1b:Private"
  ["private-db-1a"]="10.0.20.0/24:us-east-1a:Private"
  ["private-db-1b"]="10.0.21.0/24:us-east-1b:Private"
)

echo "Creating multi-tier, multi-AZ subnet architecture..."
echo ""

declare -A subnet_ids

for subnet_name in "${!subnets[@]}"; do
  IFS=':' read -r cidr az subnet_type <<< "${subnets[$subnet_name]}"
  
  echo "Creating $subnet_name ($cidr in $az)"
  
  subnet_id=$(aws ec2 create-subnet \
    --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
    --cidr-block $cidr \
    --availability-zone $az \
    --tag-specifications "ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[
      {Key=Name,Value=anihpj-$subnet_name},
      {Key=Type,Value=$subnet_type},
      {Key=Layer,Value=${subnet_name#*-}}
    ]" \
    --region $REGION \
    --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' \
    --output text)
  
  subnet_ids[$subnet_name]=$subnet_id
  echo "  ✓ Created: $subnet_id"
done

echo ""
echo "Subnet architecture created:"
echo "  Public (Web): 2 subnets across 2 AZs"
echo "  Private (App): 2 subnets across 2 AZs"
echo "  Private (DB): 2 subnets across 2 AZs"
echo "  Total: 6 subnets (18 IP ranges available)"

Example 5: Create Cache Layer Subnet with Custom DHCP Options

Create a dedicated subnet for ElastiCache (Redis/Memcached) with custom DNS and DHCP options for monitoring.

#!/bin/bash
# Create cache tier subnet with custom DHCP
VPC_ID="vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
SUBNET_CIDR="10.0.30.0/24"
AZ="us-east-1a"
REGION="us-east-1"
SUBNET_NAME="anihpj-private-cache-1a"

echo "Creating ElastiCache subnet with monitoring..."
echo ""

# Create DHCP options set for monitoring
DHCP_OPTIONS=$(aws ec2 create-dhcp-options \
  --dhcp-configuration \
    Key=domain-name,Values=ec2.internal \
    Key=domain-name-servers,Values=AmazonProvidedDNS \
    Key=ntp-servers,Values=169.254.169.123 \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=dhcp-options,Tags=[
    {Key=Name,Value=anihpj-cache-monitoring}
  ]" \
  --region $REGION \
  --query 'DhcpOptions.DhcpOptionsId' \
  --output text)

echo "✓ DHCP options created: $DHCP_OPTIONS"
echo ""

# Create the cache subnet
SUBNET_ID=$(aws ec2 create-subnet \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --cidr-block $SUBNET_CIDR \
  --availability-zone $AZ \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=subnet,Tags=[
    {Key=Name,Value=$SUBNET_NAME},
    {Key=Type,Value=Private},
    {Key=Layer,Value=Cache},
    {Key=ServiceType,Value=ElastiCache}
  ]" \
  --region $REGION \
  --query 'Subnet.SubnetId' \
  --output text)

echo "✓ Subnet created"
echo "Subnet ID: $SUBNET_ID"
echo ""

# Enable DNS resolution
aws ec2 modify-subnet-attribute \
  --subnet-id $SUBNET_ID \
  --enable-dns64 \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ DNS64 enabled for IPv6 support"
echo ""

echo "ElastiCache Configuration:"
echo "  Instance: cache.r6g.xlarge (ARM-based, 26GB)"
echo "  Engine: Redis 7.0"
echo "  Mode: Cluster mode enabled"
echo "  Nodes: 3 (shards)"
echo "  Replicas: 2 per shard"
echo "  Automatic failover: Enabled"
echo "  Encryption: In-transit and at-rest"
echo "  Subnet group: anihpj-cache-subnet-group"

create-internet-gateway

Create an internet gateway (IGW) for a VPC. An internet gateway serves as the bridge between your VPC and the internet, enabling resources in public subnets to communicate with the internet and vice versa. Each VPC can have only one IGW, but the IGW can be attached or detached from the VPC as needed.

Syntax
aws ec2 create-internet-gateway \
  [--tag-specifications 'ResourceType=internet-gateway,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=}]'] \
  [--region ]
Parameters Description
  • --tag-specifications (string): Tags to apply to the internet gateway. Format: ResourceType=internet-gateway,Tags=[{Key=Name,Value=my-igw}]
  • --region (string): AWS region where the internet gateway will be created (us-east-1, eu-west-1, etc.)
  • --dry-run (boolean): Check if the operation would succeed without actually creating the resource
Return Value
  • InternetGateway (Object): The created internet gateway with detailed information
  • InternetGatewayId (String): Unique IGW identifier (igw-xxxxxxxx)
  • Attachments (Array): List of VPCs the IGW is attached to (empty initially)
  • State (String): Current attachment state (attached, available)
  • Tags (Array): Tags applied to the internet gateway
  • OwnerId (String): AWS account ID that owns the IGW
Example 1: Create Production Internet Gateway with Naming Tags

Create an internet gateway for the production VPC with clear naming and cost allocation tags.

#!/bin/bash
# Create production internet gateway
VPC_ID="vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
REGION="us-east-1"
IGW_NAME="anihpj-prod-igw"

echo "Creating internet gateway for production VPC..."
echo "VPC ID: $VPC_ID"
echo ""

# Create the internet gateway
IGW_ID=$(aws ec2 create-internet-gateway \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=internet-gateway,Tags=[
    {Key=Name,Value=$IGW_NAME},
    {Key=Environment,Value=Production},
    {Key=ServiceType,Value=Internet-Gateway},
    {Key=CostCenter,Value=Engineering}
  ]" \
  --region $REGION \
  --query 'InternetGateway.InternetGatewayId' \
  --output text)

echo "✓ Internet gateway created"
echo "IGW ID: $IGW_ID"
echo ""

# Attach to production VPC
echo "Attaching internet gateway to VPC..."
aws ec2 attach-internet-gateway \
  --internet-gateway-id $IGW_ID \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ IGW attached to VPC"
echo ""

echo "Internet Gateway Configuration:"
echo "  Purpose: Enable public subnet internet access"
echo "  Attachment: VPC $VPC_ID"
echo "  State: attached"
echo "  High Availability: Inherent (redundant across AZs)"

Example 4: Create Multi-Region IGW Pool for Disaster Recovery

Create internet gateways in multiple regions for a disaster recovery setup, allowing quick failover to alternate regions.

#!/bin/bash
# Create multi-region IGW pool for DR
echo "Creating multi-region Internet Gateway pool..."
echo ""

declare -A regions=(
  ["us-east-1"]="vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
  ["eu-west-1"]="vpc-1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8i9"
  ["ap-southeast-1"]="vpc-2c3d4e5f6g7h8i9j0"
)

declare -A igw_ids

for region in "${!regions[@]}"; do
  vpc_id="${regions[$region]}"
  igw_name="anihpj-igw-$region"
  
  echo "Creating IGW in $region..."
  
  igw_id=$(aws ec2 create-internet-gateway \
    --tag-specifications "ResourceType=internet-gateway,Tags=[
      {Key=Name,Value=$igw_name},
      {Key=Environment,Value=Production},
      {Key=Region,Value=$region},
      {Key=DisasterRecovery,Value=Enabled}
    ]" \
    --region $region \
    --query 'InternetGateway.InternetGatewayId' \
    --output text)
  
  igw_ids[$region]=$igw_id
  echo "  ✓ Created: $igw_id"
  
  # Attach to VPC
  aws ec2 attach-internet-gateway \
    --internet-gateway-id $igw_id \
    --vpc-id $vpc_id \
    --region $region
  
  echo "  ✓ Attached to VPC: $vpc_id"
  echo ""
done

echo "Multi-Region IGW Pool Created:"
for region in "${!igw_ids[@]}"; do
  echo "  Region: $region → IGW: ${igw_ids[$region]}"
done
echo ""

echo "Disaster Recovery Configuration:"
echo "  Primary Region: us-east-1"
echo "  Secondary Region: eu-west-1"
echo "  Tertiary Region: ap-southeast-1"
echo "  RTO: < 5 minutes (DNS failover)"
echo "  RPO: < 1 minute (multi-region replication)"

Example 5: Create and Validate IGW Configuration for Compliance

Create an internet gateway with compliance tags and validate configuration for security and regulatory requirements.

#!/bin/bash
# Create compliance-tagged IGW and validate
REGION="us-east-1"
VPC_ID="vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
COMPLIANCE_IGW_NAME="anihpj-compliance-igw"

echo "Creating compliance-configured Internet Gateway..."
echo ""

# Create IGW with comprehensive compliance tags
IGW_ID=$(aws ec2 create-internet-gateway \
  --tag-specifications "ResourceType=internet-gateway,Tags=[
    {Key=Name,Value=$COMPLIANCE_IGW_NAME},
    {Key=Environment,Value=Production},
    {Key=Compliance,Value=SOC2-Type2},
    {Key=DataClassification,Value=Public},
    {Key=BackupRequired,Value=No},
    {Key=CostCenter,Value=Engineering},
    {Key=Owner,Value=CloudOps},
    {Key=Terraform,Value=True},
    {Key=CreatedDate,Value=$(date +%Y-%m-%d)},
    {Key=Version,Value=1.0}
  ]" \
  --region $REGION \
  --query 'InternetGateway.InternetGatewayId' \
  --output text)

echo "✓ IGW created: $IGW_ID"
echo ""

# Attach to VPC
aws ec2 attach-internet-gateway \
  --internet-gateway-id $IGW_ID \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ IGW attached to VPC: $VPC_ID"
echo ""

# Validate configuration
echo "=== Compliance Validation ==="
echo ""

# Check tags
echo "Tag Audit:"
aws ec2 describe-internet-gateways \
  --internet-gateway-ids $IGW_ID \
  --region $REGION \
  --query 'InternetGateways[0].Tags' \
  --output text | tr '\t' '\n'

echo ""
echo "✓ All required compliance tags present"
echo "✓ Attachment verified: $VPC_ID"
echo ""

echo "Compliance Checklist:"
echo "  ✓ IGW created and attached"
echo "  ✓ SOC2 compliance tags applied"
echo "  ✓ Owner assigned (CloudOps)"
echo "  ✓ Cost center tracked (Engineering)"
echo "  ✓ Version controlled (v1.0)"
echo "  ✓ Created date logged"

attach-internet-gateway

Attach an internet gateway to a VPC, enabling internet connectivity for resources in public subnets. The IGW must be created first, then attached to make it functional. Only one IGW can be attached to each VPC, and the attachment is instant once completed.

Syntax
aws ec2 attach-internet-gateway \
  --internet-gateway-id  \
  --vpc-id  \
  [--region ]
Parameters Description
  • --internet-gateway-id (string): The ID of the internet gateway to attach. Format: igw-xxxxxxxx
  • --vpc-id (string): The ID of the VPC to attach the internet gateway to. Format: vpc-xxxxxxxx
  • --region (string): AWS region where both the IGW and VPC exist (us-east-1, eu-west-1, etc.)
  • --dry-run (boolean): Check if the operation would succeed without actually attaching the IGW
Return Value
  • No return value: Operation returns empty response when successful
  • State change: IGW state changes from "available" to "attached"
  • VPC routing: Enables 0.0.0.0/0 routes in public route tables
  • Instance connectivity: Public subnets can now route traffic to/from internet
Example 1: Attach Production IGW to Enable ALB Internet Access

Attach the internet gateway to production VPC to enable Application Load Balancer to receive internet traffic.

#!/bin/bash
# Attach production IGW to VPC
IGW_ID="igw-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h"
VPC_ID="vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "Attaching internet gateway to production VPC..."
echo "IGW ID: $IGW_ID"
echo "VPC ID: $VPC_ID"
echo ""

# Attach the internet gateway
aws ec2 attach-internet-gateway \
  --internet-gateway-id $IGW_ID \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Internet gateway attached successfully"
echo ""

# Verify attachment
echo "Verifying IGW attachment..."
ATTACHMENT_STATE=$(aws ec2 describe-internet-gateways \
  --internet-gateway-ids $IGW_ID \
  --region $REGION \
  --query 'InternetGateways[0].Attachments[0].State' \
  --output text)

echo "Attachment state: $ATTACHMENT_STATE"
echo ""

if [ "$ATTACHMENT_STATE" = "attached" ]; then
    echo "✓ IGW successfully attached to VPC"
    echo "✓ Public subnets now have internet access"
    echo "✓ ALB can receive external traffic"
    echo "✓ NAT Gateways can route private subnet traffic"
else
    echo "✗ IGW attachment failed"
    exit 1
fi

echo ""
echo "Next steps:"
echo "  1. Configure public route table (0.0.0.0/0 → $IGW_ID)"
echo "  2. Deploy ALB in public subnets"
echo "  3. Deploy NAT Gateways for private subnet outbound"

Example 2: Attach IGW to Staging VPC with Route Table Update

Attach internet gateway to staging environment and immediately update route table for end-to-end connectivity testing.

#!/bin/bash
# Attach IGW and configure routing for staging
IGW_ID="igw-1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8i"
VPC_ID="vpc-1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8i9"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "Setting up staging VPC internet connectivity..."
echo ""

# Attach internet gateway
echo "Step 1: Attaching IGW to staging VPC"
aws ec2 attach-internet-gateway \
  --internet-gateway-id $IGW_ID \
  --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ IGW attached"
echo ""

# Find the main route table
echo "Step 2: Finding main route table"
ROUTE_TABLE_ID=$(aws ec2 describe-route-tables \
  --filters "Name=vpc-id,Values=$VPC_ID" "Name=association.main,Values=true" \
  --region $REGION \
  --query 'RouteTables[0].RouteTableId' \
  --output text)

echo "Main route table: $ROUTE_TABLE_ID"
echo ""

# Add internet route
echo "Step 3: Adding internet route (0.0.0.0/0 → IGW)"
aws ec2 create-route \
  --route-table-id $ROUTE_TABLE_ID \
  --destination-cidr-block 0.0.0.0/0 \
  --gateway-id $IGW_ID \
  --region $REGION

echo "✓ Internet route added"
echo ""

# Verify connectivity
echo "Step 4: Testing connectivity configuration"
echo "  ✓ IGW attached to VPC"
echo "  ✓ Route table configured for internet access"
echo "  ✓ All subnets now have internet routing"
echo ""

echo "Staging VPC ready for testing:"
echo "  - Deploy test instances"
echo "  - Run integration tests"
echo "  - Validate external API connections"

Example 3: Conditional IGW Attachment with Error Handling

Attach IGW with proper error handling and validation checks to prevent common attachment issues.

#!/bin/bash
# Safe IGW attachment with error handling
IGW_ID="igw-2c3d4e5f6g7h8i9j"
VPC_ID="vpc-2c3d4e5f6g7h8i9j0"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "Safe IGW attachment with validation..."
echo ""

# Function to check if IGW exists
check_igw_exists() {
    aws ec2 describe-internet-gateways \
        --internet-gateway-ids $IGW_ID \
        --region $REGION \
        --query 'InternetGateways[0].InternetGatewayId' \
        --output text 2>/dev/null
}

# Function to check if VPC exists
check_vpc_exists() {
    aws ec2 describe-vpcs \
        --vpc-ids $VPC_ID \
        --region $REGION \
        --query 'Vpcs[0].VpcId' \
        --output text 2>/dev/null
}

# Function to check if IGW is already attached
check_attachment() {
    aws ec2 describe-internet-gateways \
        --internet-gateway-ids $IGW_ID \
        --region $REGION \
        --query 'InternetGateways[0].Attachments[0].VpcId' \
        --output text 2>/dev/null
}

# Pre-flight checks
echo "Pre-flight checks:"

if [ "$(check_igw_exists)" != "$IGW_ID" ]; then
    echo "✗ IGW $IGW_ID does not exist"
    exit 1
fi
echo "✓ IGW exists"

if [ "$(check_vpc_exists)" != "$VPC_ID" ]; then
    echo "✗ VPC $VPC_ID does not exist"
    exit 1
fi
echo "✓ VPC exists"

EXISTING_VPC=$(check_attachment)
if [ "$EXISTING_VPC" != "None" ] && [ "$EXISTING_VPC" != "" ]; then
    if [ "$EXISTING_VPC" = "$VPC_ID" ]; then
        echo "ℹ IGW already attached to this VPC"
        echo "✓ No action needed"
        exit 0
    else
        echo "✗ IGW already attached to different VPC: $EXISTING_VPC"
        echo "Detach first: aws ec2 detach-internet-gateway --igw-id $IGW_ID --vpc-id $EXISTING_VPC"
        exit 1
    fi
fi
echo "✓ IGW is available for attachment"

echo ""
echo "Attaching IGW to VPC..."
aws ec2 attach-internet-gateway \
    --internet-gateway-id $IGW_ID \
    --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
    --region $REGION

if [ $? -eq 0 ]; then
    echo "✓ IGW successfully attached"
else
    echo "✗ IGW attachment failed"
    exit 1
fi

echo ""
echo "Post-attachment verification:"
ATTACHED_VPC=$(check_attachment)
if [ "$ATTACHED_VPC" = "$VPC_ID" ]; then
    echo "✓ Attachment verified"
    echo "✓ IGW $IGW_ID is now attached to VPC $VPC_ID"
else
    echo "✗ Attachment verification failed"
    exit 1
fi
Safe IGW attachment with validation... Pre-flight checks: ✓ IGW exists ✓ VPC exists ✓ IGW is available for attachment Attaching IGW to VPC... ✓ IGW successfully attached Post-attachment verification: ✓ Attachment verified ✓ IGW igw-2c3d4e5f6g7h8i9j is now attached to VPC vpc-2c3d4e5f6g7h8i9j0
# Safe IGW attachment with error handling from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost from django.utils import timezone safe_attachment = { 'igw_id': 'igw-2c3d4e5f6g7h8i9j', 'vpc_id': 'vpc-2c3d4e5f6g7h8i9j0', 'validation_passed': True, 'attachment_successful': True } print(f"Safe IGW Attachment Process") print(f"IGW ID: {safe_attachment['igw_id']}") print(f"VPC ID: {safe_attachment['vpc_id']}") print(f"Validation: {'✓ Passed' if safe_attachment['validation_passed'] else '✗ Failed'}") print(f"Attachment: {'✓ Successful' if safe_attachment['attachment_successful'] else '✗ Failed'}") print(f"") # Pre-flight validation checks validation_checks = { 'igw_existence': 'Verify IGW exists in specified region', 'vpc_existence': 'Verify VPC exists in specified region', 'igw_availability': 'Check IGW is not attached to another VPC', 'vpc_availability': 'Check VPC does not have IGW already', 'permissions': 'Verify EC2 attach permissions', 'region_consistency': 'Ensure IGW and VPC in same region' } print(f"Pre-flight Validation Checks:") for check, description in validation_checks.items(): print(f" {check}: {description}") print(f"") # IAM permissions required iam_permissions = { 'ec2:AttachInternetGateway': 'Required for attachment operation', 'ec2:DescribeInternetGateways': 'Pre-flight validation', 'ec2:DescribeVpcs': 'VPC existence validation', 'ec2:DescribeRouteTables': 'Route configuration (optional)' } print(f"Required IAM Permissions:") for permission, purpose in iam_permissions.items(): print(f" {permission}: {purpose}") # Automation best practices automation_practices = { 'idempotency': 'Check existing state before making changes', 'error_handling': 'Graceful failure with meaningful error messages', 'validation': 'Pre-flight checks before resource operations', 'logging': 'Comprehensive operation logging for debugging', 'rollback': 'Automatic rollback on failure (if applicable)', 'testing': 'Unit and integration tests for automation scripts' } print(f"\nAutomation Best Practices:") for practice, description in automation_practices.items(): print(f" {practice}: {description}") # Post-attachment validation post_validation = { 'attachment_state': 'Verify state is "attached"', 'vpc_association': 'Confirm correct VPC association', 'route_table_ready': 'Check route tables can reference IGW', 'connectivity_test': 'Test basic internet connectivity', 'monitoring_setup': 'Enable CloudWatch metrics' } print(f"\nPost-Attachment Validation:") for validation, description in post_validation.items(): print(f" {validation}: {description}") # Django deployment readiness checklist deployment_checklist = { 'network_layer': '✓ IGW attached, routes configured', 'security_layer': 'Security groups and NACLs configured', 'compute_layer': 'EC2 instances or ECS tasks ready', 'database_layer': 'RDS in private subnets', 'load_balancer': 'ALB in public subnets with IGW access', 'monitoring': 'CloudWatch, logging configured' } print(f"\nDjango Deployment Readiness:") for layer, status in deployment_checklist.items(): print(f" {layer}: {status}") print(f"\n✓ Safe IGW attachment completed") print(f"✓ All validation checks passed")
Example 4: Bulk IGW Attachment for Multi-Environment Setup

Attach multiple internet gateways to their respective VPCs for a multi-environment deployment (dev, staging, prod).

#!/bin/bash
# Bulk IGW attachment for multi-environment
REGION="us-east-1"

declare -A environments=(
    ["dev"]="igw-dev123:vpc-dev456"
    ["staging"]="igw-stg123:vpc-stg456"  
    ["prod"]="igw-prd123:vpc-prd456"
)

echo "Bulk IGW attachment for multi-environment setup..."
echo ""

for env in "${!environments[@]}"; do
    IFS=':' read -r igw_id vpc_id <<< "${environments[$env]}"
    
    echo "Environment: $env"
    echo "  IGW: $igw_id"
    echo "  VPC: $vpc_id"
    
    # Attach IGW to VPC
    aws ec2 attach-internet-gateway \
        --internet-gateway-id $igw_id \
        --vpc-id $vpc_id \
        --region $REGION
    
    if [ $? -eq 0 ]; then
        echo "  ✓ Attached successfully"
        
        # Tag the attachment for tracking
        aws ec2 create-tags \
            --resources $igw_id \
            --tags Key=AttachedTo,Value=$vpc_id Key=Environment,Value=$env \
            --region $REGION
        
        echo "  ✓ Tags updated"
    else
        echo "  ✗ Attachment failed"
        continue
    fi
    
    echo ""
done

echo "Multi-environment IGW attachment summary:"
echo "  ✓ Development VPC ready for feature testing"
echo "  ✓ Staging VPC ready for QA validation" 
echo "  ✓ Production VPC ready for live traffic"
echo ""

echo "Next steps per environment:"
echo "  Dev: Configure development route tables"
echo "  Staging: Set up load testing infrastructure"
echo "  Prod: Deploy production ALB and NAT Gateways"
Bulk IGW attachment for multi-environment setup... Environment: dev IGW: igw-dev123 VPC: vpc-dev456 ✓ Attached successfully ✓ Tags updated Environment: staging IGW: igw-stg123 VPC: vpc-stg456 ✓ Attached successfully ✓ Tags updated Environment: prod IGW: igw-prd123 VPC: vpc-prd456 ✓ Attached successfully ✓ Tags updated Multi-environment IGW attachment summary: ✓ Development VPC ready for feature testing ✓ Staging VPC ready for QA validation ✓ Production VPC ready for live traffic

Example 5: IGW Attachment with Automatic Route Table Configuration

Attach internet gateway and automatically configure public route tables for immediate internet connectivity.

#!/bin/bash
# IGW attachment with automatic route configuration
IGW_ID="igw-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h"
VPC_ID="vpc-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h8"
REGION="us-east-1"

echo "IGW attachment with automatic route table configuration..."
echo ""

# Step 1: Attach Internet Gateway
echo "Step 1: Attaching Internet Gateway"
aws ec2 attach-internet-gateway \
    --internet-gateway-id $IGW_ID \
    --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
    --region $REGION

echo "✓ IGW attached to VPC"
echo ""

# Step 2: Create dedicated public route table
echo "Step 2: Creating public route table"
PUBLIC_RT_ID=$(aws ec2 create-route-table \
    --vpc-id $VPC_ID \
    --tag-specifications "ResourceType=route-table,Tags=[
        {Key=Name,Value=anihpj-public-rt},
        {Key=Type,Value=Public}
    ]" \
    --region $REGION \
    --query 'RouteTable.RouteTableId' \
    --output text)

echo "✓ Public route table created: $PUBLIC_RT_ID"
echo ""

# Step 3: Add internet route to public route table
echo "Step 3: Adding internet route (0.0.0.0/0 → IGW)"
aws ec2 create-route \
    --route-table-id $PUBLIC_RT_ID \
    --destination-cidr-block 0.0.0.0/0 \
    --gateway-id $IGW_ID \
    --region $REGION

echo "✓ Internet route added"
echo ""

# Step 4: Associate public subnets with public route table
echo "Step 4: Associating public subnets with route table"
PUBLIC_SUBNETS=$(aws ec2 describe-subnets \
    --filters "Name=vpc-id,Values=$VPC_ID" "Name=tag:Type,Values=Public" \
    --region $REGION \
    --query 'Subnets[].SubnetId' \
    --output text)

for subnet_id in $PUBLIC_SUBNETS; do
    aws ec2 associate-route-table \
        --route-table-id $PUBLIC_RT_ID \
        --subnet-id $subnet_id \
        --region $REGION
    echo "  ✓ Associated subnet: $subnet_id"
done

echo ""
echo "Configuration complete:"
echo "  ✓ IGW attached and functional"
echo "  ✓ Public route table configured"
echo "  ✓ Internet route active (0.0.0.0/0 → IGW)"
echo "  ✓ Public subnets have internet connectivity"
echo ""

# Step 5: Verify configuration
echo "Step 5: Verifying configuration"
aws ec2 describe-route-tables \
    --route-table-ids $PUBLIC_RT_ID \
    --region $REGION \
    --query 'RouteTables[0].Routes' \
    --output table

echo ""
echo "✓ Internet connectivity ready for:"
echo "  - Application Load Balancer deployment" 
echo "  - NAT Gateway creation"
echo "  - Public instance access"
IGW attachment with automatic route table configuration... Step 1: Attaching Internet Gateway ✓ IGW attached to VPC Step 2: Creating public route table ✓ Public route table created: rtb-0123456789abcdef Step 3: Adding internet route (0.0.0.0/0 → IGW) ✓ Internet route added Step 4: Associating public subnets with route table ✓ Associated subnet: subnet-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h ✓ Associated subnet: subnet-0b2c3d4e5f6g7h8i Configuration complete: ✓ IGW attached and functional ✓ Public route table configured ✓ Internet route active (0.0.0.0/0 → IGW) ✓ Public subnets have internet connectivity Step 5: Verifying configuration ---------------------------------------------------------- | DescribeRouteTables | +-----------------+----------------+--------------------+ |DestinationCidrBlock|GatewayId |State | +-----------------+----------------+--------------------+ |10.0.0.0/16 |local |active | |0.0.0.0/0 |igw-0a1b2c3d4e5f6g7h|active | +-----------------+----------------+--------------------+

⚙️ Management & Governance

AWS Management services help you monitor, manage, and govern your infrastructure. This section covers CloudWatch for monitoring, CloudFormation for infrastructure as code, Systems Manager for operational management, and CloudTrail for auditing.

AWS CloudWatch

Monitoring and observability service for your Django application infrastructure and custom metrics

📋 CloudWatch Overview

Amazon CloudWatch provides monitoring, logging, and alerting for AWS resources and applications. Use it to track custom metrics from your anihpj Django jobpost application, set alarms for critical conditions, visualize performance data in dashboards, and gain operational insights.

Core CloudWatch Operations for Django Monitoring

put-metric-data - Send custom metrics
get-metric-statistics - Retrieve metric data
put-metric-alarm - Create alarms
describe-alarms - List alarms
delete-alarms - Remove alarms
set-alarm-state - Test alarms
list-metrics - List available metrics
get-metric-data - Query metrics
put-dashboard - Create dashboard
get-dashboard - View dashboard
list-dashboards - List dashboards
delete-dashboards - Remove dashboards

put-metric-data

Publishes custom metric data points to CloudWatch. Essential for tracking Django application-specific metrics like job posts created, user signups, API response times, and database query performance.

Syntax
aws cloudwatch put-metric-data \
  --namespace {namespace} \
  --metric-name {metric-name} \
  --value {value} \
  --dimensions Name={dimension-name},Value={dimension-value} \
  --timestamp {timestamp} \
  --unit {unit}
Parameters Description
  • --namespace (string, required): Custom namespace for your metrics. Example: "AnihpjDjango/JobPost" or "Custom/Application"
  • --metric-name (string, required): Name of the metric. Example: "JobPostsCreated", "APIResponseTime", "DatabaseQueryTime"
  • --value (double): Metric value to publish. Example: 1 (for count), 245.5 (for milliseconds)
  • --dimensions (list): Key-value pairs to identify metric variants. Example: Name=Environment,Value=production
  • --timestamp (timestamp): Time the metric was recorded (ISO 8601 format). If omitted, current time is used
  • --unit (string): Unit of measurement. Values: Seconds, Microseconds, Milliseconds, Bytes, Kilobytes, Megabytes, Gigabytes, Count, Percent, etc.
  • --metric-data (list): Send multiple metric data points in a single request (batch publishing)
Return Value
  • ResponseMetadata (Object): HTTP response metadata with RequestId and HTTPStatusCode (200 on success)
  • No explicit response body: Success indicated by HTTP 200 status
5 Detailed CloudWatch put-metric-data Examples
Example 1: Track Job Posts Created in Django Application

Send a custom metric to CloudWatch every time a new job post is created in the anihpj jobpost application.

#!/bin/bash
# Track job posts created metric
NAMESPACE="AnihpjDjango/JobPost"
METRIC_NAME="JobPostsCreated"
TIMESTAMP=$(date -u +"%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S")

# Send metric when job post is created
aws cloudwatch put-metric-data \
  --namespace "$NAMESPACE" \
  --metric-name "$METRIC_NAME" \
  --value 1 \
  --unit Count \
  --timestamp "$TIMESTAMP" \
  --dimensions Name=Environment,Value=production Name=Author,Value=user123 \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Job post creation metric sent to CloudWatch"
{ "ResponseMetadata": { "RequestId": "a1b2c3d4-e5f6-7890-abcd-ef1234567890", "HTTPStatusCode": 200, "HTTPHeaders": { "x-amzn-requestid": "a1b2c3d4-e5f6-7890-abcd-ef1234567890", "content-type": "text/xml", "content-length": "212", "date": "Fri, 17 Jan 2026 10:30:45 GMT" }, "RetryAttempts": 0 } } ✓ Job post creation metric sent to CloudWatch
# Django integration - Track job post creation metrics from jobpost.models import JobPost, Author, Skills from django.db.models.signals import post_save from django.dispatch import receiver import boto3 from datetime import datetime # Initialize CloudWatch client cloudwatch = boto3.client('cloudwatch', region_name='us-east-1') @receiver(post_save, sender=JobPost) def track_job_post_creation(sender, instance, created, **kwargs): """Send CloudWatch metric when new job post is created""" if created: try: cloudwatch.put_metric_data( Namespace='AnihpjDjango/JobPost', MetricData=[ { 'MetricName': 'JobPostsCreated', 'Value': 1, 'Unit': 'Count', 'Timestamp': datetime.utcnow(), 'Dimensions': [ {'Name': 'Environment', 'Value': 'production'}, {'Name': 'Author', 'Value': str(instance.author.id)}, {'Name': 'Location', 'Value': instance.location.city} ] } ] ) print(f"✓ Metric sent: JobPost {instance.id} created") except Exception as e: print(f"✗ CloudWatch error: {e}") # Example usage job_post = JobPost.objects.create( title="Senior Django Developer", author=Author.objects.first(), location=Location.objects.first(), status='published' ) # Output: ✓ Metric sent: JobPost 1 created
Example 2: Monitor API Response Times

Track Django API endpoint response times to monitor application performance and identify slow queries.

#!/bin/bash
# Monitor API response time
NAMESPACE="AnihpjDjango/Performance"
METRIC_NAME="APIResponseTime"
RESPONSE_TIME=245.7  # milliseconds

aws cloudwatch put-metric-data \
  --namespace "$NAMESPACE" \
  --metric-name "$METRIC_NAME" \
  --value $RESPONSE_TIME \
  --unit Milliseconds \
  --dimensions Name=Endpoint,Value=/api/jobposts Name=Method,Value=GET \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ API response time metric sent: ${RESPONSE_TIME}ms"
{ "ResponseMetadata": { "RequestId": "b2c3d4e5-f6a7-8901-bcde-f12345678901", "HTTPStatusCode": 200 } } ✓ API response time metric sent: 245.7ms
# Django middleware to track API response times from django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin import boto3 import time from datetime import datetime class CloudWatchMetricsMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin): def __init__(self, get_response): self.get_response = get_response self.cloudwatch = boto3.client('cloudwatch', region_name='us-east-1') def process_request(self, request): request.start_time = time.time() def process_response(self, request, response): if hasattr(request, 'start_time'): response_time = (time.time() - request.start_time) * 1000 # Convert to ms # Send metric to CloudWatch try: self.cloudwatch.put_metric_data( Namespace='AnihpjDjango/Performance', MetricData=[ { 'MetricName': 'APIResponseTime', 'Value': response_time, 'Unit': 'Milliseconds', 'Timestamp': datetime.utcnow(), 'Dimensions': [ {'Name': 'Endpoint', 'Value': request.path}, {'Name': 'Method', 'Value': request.method}, {'Name': 'StatusCode', 'Value': str(response.status_code)} ] } ] ) except Exception as e: print(f"CloudWatch error: {e}") return response # Add to MIDDLEWARE in settings.py: # 'jobpost.middleware.CloudWatchMetricsMiddleware', # Example output when accessing /api/jobposts: # APIResponseTime: 245.7ms for GET /api/jobposts (Status: 200)
Example 3: Batch Send Multiple Metrics

Send multiple metric data points in a single API call for efficiency - track user activity, database queries, and cache hits.

#!/bin/bash
# Batch send multiple metrics
NAMESPACE="AnihpjDjango/Application"

aws cloudwatch put-metric-data \
  --namespace "$NAMESPACE" \
  --metric-data \
    MetricName=UserSignups,Value=3,Unit=Count,Timestamp=$(date -u +"%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S"),Dimensions=[{Name=Environment,Value=production}] \
    MetricName=DatabaseQueries,Value=145,Unit=Count,Timestamp=$(date -u +"%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S"),Dimensions=[{Name=Environment,Value=production},{Name=Type,Value=SELECT}] \
    MetricName=CacheHitRate,Value=87.5,Unit=Percent,Timestamp=$(date -u +"%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%S"),Dimensions=[{Name=CacheType,Value=Redis}] \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Batch metrics sent successfully"
{ "ResponseMetadata": { "RequestId": "c3d4e5f6-a7b8-9012-cdef-123456789012", "HTTPStatusCode": 200 } } ✓ Batch metrics sent successfully Metrics published: - UserSignups: 3 (Count) - DatabaseQueries: 145 (Count) - CacheHitRate: 87.5%
# Django management command to send batch metrics from django.core.management.base import BaseCommand from django.contrib.auth.models import User from jobpost.models import JobPost, Author from django.db import connection from django.core.cache import cache import boto3 from datetime import datetime class Command(BaseCommand): help = 'Send batch metrics to CloudWatch' def handle(self, *args, **kwargs): cloudwatch = boto3.client('cloudwatch', region_name='us-east-1') # Gather metrics new_users = User.objects.filter(date_joined__date=datetime.today()).count() total_queries = len(connection.queries) cache_stats = cache.get_stats() if hasattr(cache, 'get_stats') else {} # Batch send metrics metric_data = [ { 'MetricName': 'UserSignups', 'Value': new_users, 'Unit': 'Count', 'Timestamp': datetime.utcnow(), 'Dimensions': [{'Name': 'Environment', 'Value': 'production'}] }, { 'MetricName': 'DatabaseQueries', 'Value': total_queries, 'Unit': 'Count', 'Timestamp': datetime.utcnow(), 'Dimensions': [ {'Name': 'Environment', 'Value': 'production'}, {'Name': 'Type', 'Value': 'SELECT'} ] }, { 'MetricName': 'ActiveJobPosts', 'Value': JobPost.objects.filter(status='published').count(), 'Unit': 'Count', 'Timestamp': datetime.utcnow(), 'Dimensions': [{'Name': 'Status', 'Value': 'published'}] } ] cloudwatch.put_metric_data( Namespace='AnihpjDjango/Application', MetricData=metric_data ) self.stdout.write(self.style.SUCCESS('✓ Batch metrics sent')) # Run: python manage.py send_batch_metrics
Example 4: Track Database Query Performance

Monitor Django ORM query execution times to identify slow database operations affecting the jobpost application.

#!/bin/bash
# Track database query performance
NAMESPACE="AnihpjDjango/Database"
METRIC_NAME="QueryExecutionTime"
QUERY_TIME=1250.3  # milliseconds
QUERY_TYPE="SELECT"

aws cloudwatch put-metric-data \
  --namespace "$NAMESPACE" \
  --metric-name "$METRIC_NAME" \
  --value $QUERY_TIME \
  --unit Milliseconds \
  --dimensions \
    Name=QueryType,Value=$QUERY_TYPE \
    Name=Table,Value=jobpost_jobpost \
    Name=Complexity,Value=Join \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Database query metric sent: ${QUERY_TIME}ms"
{ "ResponseMetadata": { "RequestId": "d4e5f6a7-b8c9-0123-def1-234567890123", "HTTPStatusCode": 200 } } ✓ Database query metric sent: 1250.3ms
# Django database query performance monitoring from django.db import connection from django.db.backends.utils import CursorWrapper import boto3 import time from datetime import datetime class CloudWatchQueryMonitor: def __init__(self): self.cloudwatch = boto3.client('cloudwatch', region_name='us-east-1') def track_query(self, sql, duration_ms, query_type='SELECT'): """Send query performance metric to CloudWatch""" # Determine table from SQL table = 'unknown' if 'FROM' in sql.upper(): parts = sql.upper().split('FROM')[1].strip().split() if parts: table = parts[0].replace('`', '').replace('"', '') try: self.cloudwatch.put_metric_data( Namespace='AnihpjDjango/Database', MetricData=[ { 'MetricName': 'QueryExecutionTime', 'Value': duration_ms, 'Unit': 'Milliseconds', 'Timestamp': datetime.utcnow(), 'Dimensions': [ {'Name': 'QueryType', 'Value': query_type}, {'Name': 'Table', 'Value': table}, {'Name': 'Complexity', 'Value': 'Join' if 'JOIN' in sql.upper() else 'Simple'} ] } ] ) except Exception as e: print(f"CloudWatch metric error: {e}") # Example: Monitor complex query from jobpost.models import JobPost monitor = CloudWatchQueryMonitor() start = time.time() # Complex query with joins jobs = JobPost.objects.select_related('author', 'location').prefetch_related('required_skills') jobs_list = list(jobs.filter(status='published')[:100]) duration_ms = (time.time() - start) * 1000 print(f"Query executed in {duration_ms:.2f}ms") # Output: Query executed in 1250.30ms # Metric sent to CloudWatch with table and complexity dimensions
Example 5: Monitor Custom Business Metrics

Track business-specific metrics like skills demand, location popularity, and author activity for the jobpost application.

#!/bin/bash
# Track business metrics
NAMESPACE="AnihpjDjango/Business"

# Skills demand metric
aws cloudwatch put-metric-data \
  --namespace "$NAMESPACE" \
  --metric-name "SkillDemand" \
  --value 45 \
  --unit Count \
  --dimensions Name=Skill,Value=Python Name=Period,Value=Daily \
  --region us-east-1

# Location popularity
aws cloudwatch put-metric-data \
  --namespace "$NAMESPACE" \
  --metric-name "LocationPopularity" \
  --value 128 \
  --unit Count \
  --dimensions Name=City,Value=SanFrancisco Name=Period,Value=Weekly \
  --region us-east-1

# Author activity
aws cloudwatch put-metric-data \
  --namespace "$NAMESPACE" \
  --metric-name "AuthorActivity" \
  --value 23 \
  --unit Count \
  --dimensions Name=AuthorID,Value=author_123 Name=Action,Value=PostsCreated \
  --region us-east-1

echo "✓ Business metrics sent to CloudWatch"
{ "ResponseMetadata": { "RequestId": "e5f6a7b8-c9d0-1234-ef12-345678901234", "HTTPStatusCode": 200 } } ✓ Business metrics sent to CloudWatch Metrics tracking: - SkillDemand: Python (45 job posts today) - LocationPopularity: San Francisco (128 posts this week) - AuthorActivity: author_123 (23 posts created)
# Django scheduled task to track business metrics from django.core.management.base import BaseCommand from jobpost.models import JobPost, Skills, Location, Author from django.db.models import Count from datetime import datetime, timedelta import boto3 class Command(BaseCommand): help = 'Send business metrics to CloudWatch' def handle(self, *args, **kwargs): cloudwatch = boto3.client('cloudwatch', region_name='us-east-1') timestamp = datetime.utcnow() # Track skills demand today = datetime.today().date() skills_demand = JobPost.objects.filter( created_at__date=today ).values('required_skills__name').annotate(count=Count('id')) for skill_data in skills_demand: skill_name = skill_data['required_skills__name'] count = skill_data['count'] cloudwatch.put_metric_data( Namespace='AnihpjDjango/Business', MetricData=[{ 'MetricName': 'SkillDemand', 'Value': count, 'Unit': 'Count', 'Timestamp': timestamp, 'Dimensions': [ {'Name': 'Skill', 'Value': skill_name or 'Unknown'}, {'Name': 'Period', 'Value': 'Daily'} ] }] ) # Track location popularity last_week = today - timedelta(days=7) location_stats = JobPost.objects.filter( created_at__date__gte=last_week ).values('location__city').annotate(count=Count('id')) for loc_data in location_stats: city = loc_data['location__city'] count = loc_data['count'] cloudwatch.put_metric_data( Namespace='AnihpjDjango/Business', MetricData=[{ 'MetricName': 'LocationPopularity', 'Value': count, 'Unit': 'Count', 'Timestamp': timestamp, 'Dimensions': [ {'Name': 'City', 'Value': city or 'Unknown'}, {'Name': 'Period', 'Value': 'Weekly'} ] }] ) self.stdout.write(self.style.SUCCESS('✓ Business metrics sent')) # Schedule with cron: 0 0 * * * python manage.py send_business_metrics
